(Hong Kong) The Civil and Finance Departments jointly drafted measures to prohibit gambling. Miscellaneous gambling will be prohibited from September, fan-tan from October, and entertainment gambling such as mahjong from New Year's Day next year. The decision will be submitted to the provincial government on the 18th for approval. The Finance Department is preparing to establish a Financial Reform Committee, inviting central financial officials and Guangdong economic experts as members. The Fourth Route Army's military pay will be changed to be issued in silver dollars. (17th Special Dispatch)

After Fiercely Attacking Hong Kong and Guangdong, the Center of the Typhoon Reaches Nanning; Extremely Heavy Losses on Land and Sea in Hong Kong and Guangdong; The Pearl River Bursts its Banks, Flooding Both Sides; The Force of the Northern Advance Gradually Decreases; It Will Disappear in Yunnan Province Within Days 16

(Hong Kong) Hong Kong and Macau were hit by a typhoon this morning, the 17th. The intensity was extremely strong and lasted for six hours before stopping, causing considerable losses, with scores of people injured or killed. (17th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Central Meteorological Observatory reported at 2 PM on the 17th that the typhoon had reached the Guangdong-Kwangsi area, with its center near Nanning. The wind force is gradually decreasing, and it is continuing to move north, with a tendency to dissipate in Yunnan Province within a day or two. (17th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Hong Kong was hit by a typhoon and rainstorm this morning, the 17th, lasting for seven hours. The wind force was fierce, unseen in recent years. The losses on land and sea were quite heavy, including the collapse of more than twenty buildings, over a hundred people dead or injured, and the sinking of twelve ships and boats. A customs patrol vessel was blown ashore in Kowloon Bay, and all swimming sheds were destroyed. (17th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) According to the Central Meteorological Observatory, the typhoon that struck Hong Kong made landfall at 6 AM on the 17th, 50 kilometers southwest of Hong Kong, with the highest wind force. Gale-force winds and rain occurred throughout Hong Kong. The typhoon is currently continuing to advance to the northwest-west at a speed of 30 kilometers, and within 24 hours it will reach Kwangsi, Guangdong, southern Fujian, southern Jiangxi, and southern Hunan, all of which will experience gale-force winds and rain. (17th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Guangzhou) At 2 AM this morning, the 17th, a typhoon blew into the city, with extremely rampant force. It subsided somewhat around 11 AM. Many shop signs, awnings, and glass windows and doors were destroyed. Houses also collapsed. Many boats on the river were blown over because they could not avoid the wind. The long embankment road along the Pearl River was submerged by torrential waves, but fortunately, it receded soon. People and animals were injured. Statistics on the losses throughout the city are currently unavailable, but the number must be very large. (17th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Guangzhou) At 5 PM this afternoon, the typhoon raged violently here, causing further significant damage to houses and trees. The water in the Pearl River rose sharply, flooding both banks. The riverside and some other streets were flooded, and low-lying areas became a waterlogged country. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Last night, a typhoon struck Hong Kong and its surrounding areas with great force. It is feared that some shipowners who did not have time to seek shelter in the harbor and impoverished residents on land have suffered some loss of life. Hong Kong has suffered a full-force typhoon strike for perhaps the first time in recent years. According to reports, the final warning signal for this typhoon was hoisted at 12:30 AM. Fifteen minutes later, warning cannons were fired to announce the arrival of the typhoon. Consequently, many ships in the harbor weighed anchor and went to Shelter Bay to take temporary shelter. Most of the smaller boats had received warnings earlier in the afternoon and were safely berthed in shelters. The force of the typhoon has not abated by this morning. A Reuters reporter traveled throughout the city and saw desolation everywhere and witnessed two corpses crushed by rubble. Hospital ambulances were extremely busy transporting the injured. The streets were filled with various destroyed objects, such as broken tiles, collapsed walls, iron sheets, and blown-down trees. Traffic in several places was completely blocked. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) During the wind and rain, a landslide occurred in Stanley District. It is reported that about a hundred Chinese were buried alive. It is hoped that some can be rescued. The Taikoo Company's "Xin Ning" (2,555 tons) sailed to Shelter Bay last night to take shelter from the wind and is now stranded on Nineton Hill. There are a total of forty passengers on board, but it is not yet known if there are any foreigners. The crew are British sailors and Chinese sailors. The ship was hit by huge waves, and the situation is quite dangerous. Hong Kong has dispatched a small tugboat to try to carry the people on board to safety. Furthermore, the freighter "Kai Pi La Luo" is stranded in Kowloon Bay. The ship has been idle for a long time, and it is now believed that there is only one caretaker on board. At 10 AM this morning, the tail of the typhoon was still raging in Hong Kong. Staff of various firms, including Reuters, are temporarily trapped in Kowloon. However, the weather is gradually improving, and ferry boats are attempting to cross the sea. It is expected that everything can return to normal by this afternoon. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

(Manila) Last week, a typhoon blew through northern Luzon. The government survey vessel "Fa Suo Mo" was wrecked, but the sailors on board were rescued. Several other small boats are missing, and some people have died. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

(Guangzhou) At 3 AM this morning, Guangzhou was hit by a typhoon unseen in many years, toppling many houses and sinking dozens of sampans. Countless large trees were uprooted. It is reported that a total of ten people in the city died, and the number of those who died in the water has not yet been determined. Electric lights and telegraph lines were mostly blown down, so the electricity supply was completely cut off. The losses from this typhoon will be huge. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The Taikoo Company's "Xin Ning" steamer (2,555 tons), after being blown aground by the typhoon on Nineton Hill in Shelter Bay, is said to have completely broken up. The Chinese sailors and British crew on board, as well as more than forty passengers, were fortunately rescued by the British military authorities and the water police and escaped from danger. Around 5 AM this morning, the wind force greatly diminished, and all signals were lowered. The harbor has returned to its usual state, but the damage caused by the typhoon is quite considerable. Many houses have been blown down, and countless trees have fallen to the ground. Many wooden boats have also sunk. The number of deaths on land is about twenty, but the number of casualties on the water is still unknown. As for the ships that were blown aground by the typhoon, in addition to the aforementioned "Xin Ning," there are several others. The merchant ship "Ha Te Lai Qi Ya" is aground on a football field on Stonemasons' Island. The customs patrol vessel "Hai Teng" has also been grounded in Kowloon Bay. The yacht "Xue Na Du A" of the American millionaire Fang En Si Tuo Ke and the Java Company's mail steamer "Tie Ru Ba Da Ke" were blown by the typhoon and drifted with the current, but fortunately, proper measures were taken, and they did not suffer any losses. The British ship "Ta Er Ma," which was berthed in Shelter Bay, was also blown by the wind and dragged anchor, but fortunately, the shipping industry was calm and held steady, and disaster was avoided. From time to time, news of disasters and reported deaths from various places near Hong Kong come. It is said that the entire village of Quan Sha in Kowloon has actually been completely destroyed, and many villagers have been killed or injured. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

National Election Headquarters Explains Doubts Regarding Chamber of Commerce Elections 23

(Nanjing) The General Office for the Election of Representatives to the National Assembly stated that requests for clarification regarding doubts about Chamber of Commerce elections have been flooding in recently, amounting to four items: (1) How should store members of various trade associations be recorded in the organization roster? (2) Who should exercise the voting rights of the aforementioned members? (3) Does each store have one vote, or does each representative have one vote? (4) Do store members of the Chamber of Commerce have the right to nominate and elect? The General Office has recently provided explanations separately: (1) The store name and the name, age, native place, and years of engagement in the occupation of its representative should be recorded. (2) In accordance with Article 24, Paragraph 2 of the Election Law, the store is regarded as a trade association group member, and its representative is regarded as a member of that member group. (3) Each representative has one vote. (4) Store members of the Chamber of Commerce are allowed to have their member representatives have the right to vote, but they do not have the right to nominate candidates. (17th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Our country's commissioners Liang Yuchun and Yin Mingde plan to depart from Nanjing for Yunnan in October. The League of Nations neutral commissioners are scheduled to leave Geneva at the end of September. (17th Special Dispatch)

International Commercial Telegram

Special Reuters Commercial Telegram, August 17 37

Gold and Silver

The London gold price rose one penny today to 138 shillings and 5 pence.

The London silver market was stable today. The current and forward prices were unchanged at 19.5 pence. India bought and China sold. Trading was narrow.

The Mountrie silver market opened steadily today. The December futures price was unchanged at 470-45.00.

Exchange Rates

The British-American exchange market in London this morning was quiet. The pound was slightly weaker against the dollar. The British-American exchange rate opened at 5.026875 yuan, down 0.03125 from Saturday's close. It continued to fall by 125 an hour later to 5.0256115 yuan. The price was unchanged at 1 PM.

Securities

The New York stock market was mixed this morning. Trading was thin, and sentiment was still stable. Encouraging commercial news stabilized the market. Demand for railway and oil stocks was strong, while steel, copper, and public utility stocks fell slightly under speculative pressure near noon. The New York stock prices are listed on the left.

Cotton and Wheat

Liverpool wheat opened steady today, as expected, but prices fell sharply after local parties settled in large numbers. Subsequent price fluctuations were minimal. At 1 PM, the October price was 75 lower than Saturday's close at 7 shillings and 4.125 pence.

Liverpool cotton futures were stable today. At 1 PM, the October price rose by 9 pounds to 6.33.

New York cotton opened higher this morning due to bullish weather reports and stable Liverpool prices. However, trading seemed thinner. At noon, the October price was 11.80, up 9 pounds from Saturday's close.

Chicago wheat futures soared today due to good purchases by peers and speculators. At noon, the September price was 111.625, up 1.375 from Saturday's close. The grain market was firm due to speculative buying. At noon, the September price was up 2.25 from Saturday's close.

Rubber

The London rubber market was quiet today. At 1 PM, the transaction price for October-December was 7.625 pence, down from Friday's close.

The New York rubber market was sluggish and uninspired today. It opened lower due to long liquidation, but rebounded slightly due to some peer purchases. At noon, the September price was 16.18, a net drop of seven pounds from Friday's close. The New York commodity prices are listed on the left.

Japanese Foreign Ministry and Military Review Policy Towards Russia; Ambassador Ohta Reports to Prime Minister to Open Up the Current Diplomatic Situation Between the Two Countries 38

(Nanjing) The lineup of Japanese diplomacy towards Russia has been refreshed with the appointment of Former Resolution Officer Shigemitsu and the transfer of Attaché Sakō to Russia. Foreign Minister Arita plans to take this opportunity to ask the new and old ambassadors to Russia and the heads of the army and navy to review Japan's diplomatic policy towards Russia and decide on the policy to be adopted in the future based on Ambassador Ohta's report. According to Ambassador Ohta's report, the Soviet Russian government still does not abandon its hope for a Japanese-Russian non-aggression treaty four years ago and proposes this issue whenever the opportunity arises. Furthermore, it is actively strengthening its military preparations in the Far East. Regarding the issue of determining the Russian-Manchukuo border, the Russian side only expressed some sincerity. As for revising fisheries and other issues, it did not express a friendly attitude. Although Soviet Russian Defense Commissar Voroshilov stated that Soviet Russia has no intention of challenging, this statement did not have any impact on the Japanese people. Therefore, although the fundamental spirit of Japan's future policy towards Russia will not change, it will seek to open up the current diplomatic situation between the two countries and develop its situation. (17th Allied News Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Japan's fundamental diplomatic policy towards the Soviet Union is now being carefully reviewed on the occasion of Ambassador Ohta's return home. As a result of the meeting of the three ministries of Foreign Affairs, Army, and Navy, the basic tone of Japanese diplomacy towards the Soviet Union, which is to solve the pending issues such as the Soviet-Manchukuo border issue and Japanese-Soviet fisheries negotiations first, and at the same time demand the withdrawal of the 300,000 Red Army concentrated in the Far East, will be the main focus, so this matter is extremely important. (17th Allied News Dispatch)

(Nanjing) After Japanese Ambassador to the Soviet Union Ohta returned to his country on the 13th of this month, he visited Prime Minister Hirota at his official residence on the 17th and reported in detail on the recent relations between European countries and the Soviet Union, Soviet industry and national defense, especially the Soviet Union's military preparations in the Far East, the Soviet government's feelings towards Japan, the Soviet-Manchukuo border issue, and Soviet-Mongolian relations, and made important suggestions regarding Japan's policy towards the Soviet Union. (17th Allied News Dispatch)

(Nanjing) After the Japanese Ambassador to the Soviet Union, Ohta, returned to Tokyo, the newspapers carried his remarks, saying, "Japan places its relations with the Soviet Union at the center of its entire diplomatic policy, shouting that the Soviet Union threatens the Far East, while the Soviet Union's attitude towards Japan is quite calm. Soviet responsible leaders have stated that the Soviet Union is not in a provocative position towards any power, whether now or in the future. They feel that there is no problem between the Soviet Union and Japan that can only be resolved by force. The Soviet Union's participation in the League of Nations has been an obvious success, and the Soviet Union's friendship with Britain has also been a great achievement." Ohta will meet with Foreign Minister Arita to report in detail on the Soviet situation and make some suggestions for improving Japanese-Soviet relations. (16th TASS Dispatch)

(Nanjing) According to semi-official sources, the basic points of the policy towards the Soviet Union recently decided by the Foreign Affairs, Army, and Navy Ministers' Conference are to resolve various pending issues and not to advocate concluding a non-aggression treaty as a prerequisite for other negotiations. Japan will also demand that the Soviet Union withdraw the 300,000 troops stationed in the Far East, in other words, (1) the Red Army within a certain distance from the Manchurian border should be withdrawn, and (2) a demilitarized zone should be established in accordance with the spirit of the Portsmouth Treaty. As for the issue of permanent peace in the Far East, it should be discussed after the above points are negotiated. Regarding the future of Japanese-Soviet negotiations to resolve pending issues, the responsible parties also acknowledge that problems such as border conflicts, boundary affairs, fisheries, and oil are difficult to eliminate. (17th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Four Japanese Navy Aircraft Fly to Qiqihar; Russian Authorities Inspect Leningrad's Air Defense 39

(Leningrad) Defense Commissar General Voroshilov, accompanied by Generals Igorov and Budani, arrived in Leningrad yesterday and jointly reviewed Leningrad's air defense, air raid drills, and poison gas drills with Communist Party Provincial Committee Secretary Zhdanov. (16th TASS Dispatch)

(Tokorozawa) Four new-style reconnaissance aircraft from the Tokorozawa Air Unit conducted a long-distance flight to Qiqihar on the 17th. The weather was bad and the visibility was low that day, but the eight crew members, divided into aircraft, departed from Tokorozawa Airfield at 5 AM, arrived at Tachiarai at 11:30 AM, refueled, and left the area again at noon to continue flying, scheduled to arrive in Qiqihar within the 18th. (17th Allied News Dispatch)

Horse Race and Hirota Agreement: Determining National Policy Guidelines; Prioritizing National Defense; Naval Five-Year Expenditure of One Billion Yuan 40

(Nanjing) Finance Minister Baba visited Prime Minister Hirota at 10:50 AM today. Regarding the preliminary work for deciding national policy, he had conducted individual consultations with each minister other than the military ministers. He reported the details of these consultations and, based on their results, presented his future policy directions, requesting the Prime Minister's consideration. The Prime Minister immediately approved the Ministry of Finance's recommendations to determine the fundamental national policy. Therefore, the Finance Minister will soon meet with Army Minister Terauchi, Navy Minister Nagano, and others to understand the military's intentions and seek their understanding. Simultaneously, the three top cabinet officials will make further efforts to reach a compromise with relevant cabinet members. The fundamental direction of the national policy has been largely agreed upon as follows:

(1) Each ministry must compile a budget summary that aligns with revenue plans to determine national policy.

(2) National policy decisions must prioritize national defense spending.

(3) Broadly defined national defense issues, such as fuel policies, must be resolved in favor of national defense.

(4) Rural issues related to local financial allocations and national insurance policies, which contribute to stabilizing people’s livelihood, must be respected.

(5) Trade policies that promote industry should be implemented within the limits of available revenue. (17th, Domei News Agency)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance's review of each ministry's important national policies is nearly complete due to Finance Minister Baba's individual consultations with each ministry's ministers. The first step of preparatory work is completed. Prime Minister Hirota plans to meet with Finance Minister Baba around the 18th to decide on the highest-level guidelines for selecting important national policies. As a result of the Finance Minister's negotiations with each ministry's ministers in recent days, a mutual understanding has been reached. The Ministry of Finance will provide a massive amount of 150 million yuan to fund each ministry’s important national policies (excluding the Army and Navy) and general new projects. Therefore, the national policy issues are likely to be resolved satisfactorily. It is reported that the government has decided to categorize the national policy proposals submitted by each ministry into two types: important national policies and important new facilities. The general outline is as follows: (A) Important National Policy Matters:

(1) The Ministry of Interior's institutionalization of the local finance grant system and national health policy.

(2) The Ministry of Education's proposed reform of the compulsory education system.

(3) The Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry's debt restructuring plan for rural areas.

(4) The Ministry of Commerce and Industry's fuel policy and trade policy.

(5) The Ministry of Communications' nationalization of electricity and aviation policies.

(B) Important New Facility Matters:

(1) The Ministry of Interior's five-year civil engineering plan.

(2) The Ministry of Justice's regulation and facilities improvement.

(3) The Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry's disaster insurance and merino sheep policy.

(4) The Ministry of Commerce and Industry's small and medium enterprise assistance plan.

(5) The Ministry of Communications' maritime policy.

(6) The Ministry of Colonial Affairs' immigration plan for Manchuria. (17th, Domei News Agency)

(Nanjing) Prime Minister Hirota is scheduled to discuss national policy issues with Finance Minister Baba around the 18th. The government has already established the principles of strengthening national defense, establishing fiscal stability, promoting industry and trade, and stabilizing the people's livelihood as the foundation for deciding national policy. Regarding the reform of administrative structure, the Army advocates establishing an organization to plan, control, and coordinate national policy in place of the existing Investigation Bureau, appointing its head as a minister without portfolio. It also strongly advocates establishing a new Ministry of Aviation to promote the civil aviation industry. However, Prime Minister Hirota's attitude is negative. He believes there is no need to reorganize the Investigation Bureau and appoint a minister without portfolio, and that civil aviation issues can be resolved by expanding the Aviation Bureau of the Ministry of Communications. (17th, Domei News Agency)

(Nanjing) In order to cope with the international situation after the expiration of the naval treaties next year and to ensure the stability of national defense, the initial-year budget request estimate for the new national defense enhancement plan was finalized on the 17th. After Navy Minister Nagano approved it that day, it was submitted to the Ministry of Finance. The required expenses for the Navy's new national defense enhancement plan, which includes the construction of urgently needed capital ship replacements, auxiliary warships, and the increase of air squadrons, amount to 1 billion yuan, which is a regular request for a five-year continuous project. Further plans will be formulated and requested later after considering the development of the international situation and other factors. The Navy's budget estimate request for next year, including the initial-year expenses required for the new military enhancement plan, totals 770 million yuan, including a base budget of 430 million yuan and a new request of 340 million yuan. The main items in the new request are capital ship replacement construction costs, auxiliary warship construction costs, air squadron expansion costs, new warship maintenance costs, air squadron reorganization and maintenance costs, land and sea facility improvement costs, large-scale exercise costs, and other necessary expenses. (17th, Domei News Agency)

US Economic Policy: Not Inclined Towards Self-Sufficiency and Isolation; Pacific Society Continues Meeting 41

Yosemite, California, USA. The Pacific Society continued its meeting today. American expert Locke Owe declared at the conference that the Roosevelt administration's commercial policy is not inclined towards economic self-sufficiency in pursuit of economic independence during wartime. On the contrary, if international trade were to be interrupted, it would cause severe economic disruption in the United States and lead to greater control over agricultural and industrial production. For this reason, the US government must promote international trade. (17th, Guomin News Agency)

American Invention: High-Speed Torpedo Boat 42

Stamford, Connecticut, USA. A new type of torpedo boat, 50 feet long, 13 feet wide, and 10 feet deep, with a hull painted in silver and red, recently underwent final trials in this port. Its speed exceeds that of any warship. The boat has four engines with a total of 1,200 horsepower, a speed of 50 miles per hour, and agile maneuverability, making it the latest weapon of the United States. This boat was originally a type of lifeboat, but it is said that it can be converted into a torpedo boat for night attacks on enemy ships. It can accommodate four crew members, and each side can carry two tons of torpedoes. No cannon or machine gun can sink this boat. The boat can also be carried on top of capital ships and launched at any time like an airplane to attack enemy ships within 300 miles, and it can escape from the enemy ship's range within minutes after launching torpedoes. Report on the Achievements of the Rockefeller Foundation in China (Continued) 63

— Gu Huimin

The Medical Education Association of the Ministry of Education received a grant of 2,350 yuan in national currency from the Foundation. As a result, the Ministry of Education was able to unify the Medical, Midwifery, and Nursing Committees and establish a technical subcommittee to determine better teaching standards. The Medical Committee has a publishing department that publishes a medical monthly and plans to edit textbooks and reference books on medicine, nursing, and midwifery. A planned teacher training program has been launched. The Ministry of Education provides 11 scholarships for various institutions, also funded by the Foundation. In addition, the Medical Committee has also established 13 scholarships specifically for training public health [something unclear] to become leaders in [something unclear]. Peking Union Medical College has been designated to undertake this training work.

Nanjing Agricultural Plan

China is an agricultural country, with 85% of the population relying on farmland and its products for survival. Therefore, the rural problem cannot be ignored. The Foundation subsidizes institutions in Nanjing, including Jinling University, Central University, and the Agricultural Experiment Station.

The Department of Economics [something unclear] of Jinling University received a grant of $5,500 USD and 55,000 yuan in national currency from the Foundation, while the Department of Natural Sciences received 17,500 yuan in national currency. Jinling University has a long history of achievement in agricultural science, and its research on rural economy and wheat is well-known. The Foundation aims to encourage the management of agricultural product prices and the organization of rural commerce.

The College of Agriculture of Central University received a grant of 34,600 yuan in national currency from the Foundation to promote research on animal husbandry and veterinary disease prevention medicine, which is a much-needed talent and should be encouraged.

The Agricultural Experiment Station of the Ministry of Industry received a grant of 34,300 yuan in national currency from the Foundation to promote locust control, encourage research in economic entomology, hire excellent staff, purchase suitable equipment, and provide facilities for scientific research on agricultural problems. The station has already published many publications.

Scholarships

In 1935, the Rockefeller Foundation awarded a total of $57,500 USD in scholarships in China, of which $20,000 USD was allocated in 1934 and $37,500 USD was allocated in 1935. Foreign scholarships accounted for $22,000 USD, while domestic scholarships accounted for $35,000 USD. There is a growing trend to focus on domestic scholarships. There are 140 domestic scholarships, with a majority focusing on the training of rural revitalization personnel, which is also a new shift. The distribution of domestic scholarships awarded by the Rockefeller Foundation in China in 1935 is listed below:

1935 Domestic Scholarship Allocation Table

Institution Name | Number of Recipients | Subject of Study | Number of Recipients

---|---|---|---

Nanjing Health Department | 52 | Social Sciences | 29

Dingxian Mass Education Promotion Association | 37 | Public Health Nursing | 29

Medical Education Committee | 24 | Medical School and Nursing Management | 24

Nankai University | 11 | Public Health Staff Course | 23

National Economic Council, Cooperative Affairs Committee | 5 | Education | 21

Yenching University | 5 | Sanitary Engineering | 7

Beijing Municipal Health Bureau | 2 | Natural Sciences | 4

Qilu University | 2 | Public Health Technician Course | 3

National Zhejiang University | 1 | |

National Geological Survey | 1 | |

Total | 140 | Total | 140

Grants

In 1935, the total amount of grants for research and development was $25,000 USD, of which $15,000 USD was allocated in 1934 and $10,000 USD was allocated in 1935. The actual amount spent was $17,290 USD. There were 16 research projects subsidized, of which 2 were in economics, 6 were in medicine and public health, 7 were in natural sciences, and 1 was in rural training. Each subsidy cannot exceed $3,000 USD. Small subsidies are more effective, and although the amount is small, they are still related to China's revitalization plan.

The staff of the Rockefeller Foundation China Office are: Selskar M. Gunn (Vice President of the Foundation), Brian R. Dyer, John R. Grant (End)

Japanese Dignitaries Gather in Tianjin for Conferences on North China; Tadashi and Kawagoe are the Focus of the Meetings 64

Tianjin Dispatch: With the resolution of the Guangdong-Guangxi problem, the Japanese side believes that an opportunity has arrived to adjust its diplomacy towards China. At the same time, it also believes that the situation in North China will undergo serious changes under the instructions of the central government. Therefore, civil and military dignitaries have either come north from Shanghai or been dispatched from Japan to gather in Tianjin and convene the so-called "Conference on Sino-Japanese Diplomacy and Economic Cooperation." In addition to Ambassador Kawagoe, the individuals who have come to Tianjin to participate in this conference include Ishimoto Kenji, Director of the South Manchuria Railway (SMR); Sogō Shinji, President of the China Development Company; Kagesa, former Section Chief of the First Section of the Military Affairs Bureau of the Ministry of the Army; Nakamura, Section Chief of the First Section of the Military Affairs Bureau of the Ministry of the Navy; and Ōta, an official of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The newly appointed Chief of Staff of the North China Garrison Army, Hashimoto Gun, also arrived on the 17th with the newly appointed staff officer of the military intelligence team, Tada, and the newly appointed head of the Taiyuan Special Agency, Kōno, in order to attend the meeting. The heads of the North China Special Agencies belonging to the Garrison Army, including Songshishi, the head of the Beiping Special Agency; Hamada, the deputy head of the Beiping Special Agency; Konoe, the military attaché of the embassy in Beiping; Kawabe, the brigade commander of the infantry brigade; Hosoki, the head of the Tongzhou Special Agency; Kuwabara, the head of the Shanhaiguan Special Agency; Ōmoto, the head of the Zhangjiakou Special Agency; and Hayama, the head of the Suiyuan Special Agency, were all summoned by telegram and arrived successively on the evening of the 16th and the morning of the 17th. The sequence of the conference is roughly as follows: (1) At 2:00 PM on the 17th, Commander Tadashi of the Japanese Army and Ambassador Kawagoe will serve as the center to convene the so-called "Important Conference on the Current Situation," with the staff of the military headquarters and the Consul-General in Tianjin, Tajiri, and other officials also participating. The agenda includes: 1. The issue of adjusting Sino-Japanese relations; 2. The issue of economic cooperation; 3. The serious issue of the situation in North China. First, opinions will be exchanged, and then detailed studies will be conducted to achieve concrete results. (2) Representatives from the Army, Navy, and Ministry of Foreign Affairs, including Kagesa, Nakamura, and Ōta, will serve as the center to hold a conference at the Japanese Army Headquarters in Haiguang Temple on the afternoon of the 18th. Tadashi and Kawagoe will lead the staff of the military headquarters, the heads of special agencies from various places, and consuls from various parts of North China to attend. The agenda includes: 1. The three representatives will listen to reports from the Japanese Army Headquarters, the embassy, and the naval attaché in Tianjin on recent events in North China; 2. The three representatives will convey the opinions of the Army, Navy, and Ministry of Foreign Affairs on diplomatic politics after the changes in the Chinese situation and provide instructions; 3. The three parties will discuss emergency measures for the current situation. (3) Kawagoe will serve as the center to convene a conference of consuls stationed in various parts of North China at the Tianjin Consulate-General on the morning of the 20th or the morning of the 22nd. The agenda includes: 1. Reports from the consuls in various parts of North China; 2. Research on the issue of economic cooperation; 3. The issue of changes in the political situation in North China; (4) The opinion of adjusting Sino-Japanese relations. (4) The Chief of Staff of the Japanese Army Headquarters, Hashimoto Gun, will serve as the center to convene a conference of military attachés stationed in various parts of North China, which is scheduled to be held around the 22nd. The agenda includes: 1. The military attachés will report on the current situation; 2. Research on the Suiyuan problem; 3. Hashimoto will convey the opinions of the General Staff Headquarters on the current situation; 4. The issue of cooperation in North China's economic development. The above four types of conferences will be convened separately, but their goals are the same and they each have their own advantages.

Kawagoe Shigeru is scheduled to arrive in Tianjin from Qingdao by plane at 11:15 AM on the 17th. He will be accompanied by Nishiharu Hiko, the Consul-General in Qingdao; Arino, the Consul-General in Jinan; Ohara, the secretary of the embassy; and Hoshino. After landing, they are scheduled to rest at the Changmao Inn in the Japanese concession. At 2:00 PM, they will visit Tadashi at the Haiguang Temple Headquarters and attend the conference convened there. At 7:00 PM, the acting Consul-General in Tianjin, Tajiri, will host a banquet at his official residence in the British concession, inviting consuls from various places to accompany him. On the morning of the 18th, Kawagoe will visit various parties and meet with various staff members of the garrison army. In the afternoon, he will attend the conference convened by representatives of the Army, Navy, and Ministry of Foreign Affairs. On the 19th, he will meet with various Chinese and Japanese figures to deeply discuss the current situation and opinions on Sino-Japanese economic cooperation. Many prominent figures from the opposition party have been invited to attend. The North China consular conference will be held on the 20th. On the 21st and 22nd, he will leave Tianjin for Beiping to visit Zhu Jichuan and stay for a few days before returning south. He will visit [something unclear] in Jinan for a talk. At the beginning of next month, he will return to Nanjing from Shanghai to [something unclear] negotiate with the authorities on the results obtained from the North China [something unclear] conference and begin [something unclear] discussing the adjustment of Sino-Japanese relations and economic [something unclear]. The North China [something unclear] affairs who are attending this [something unclear] conference, in addition to the consuls-general of Jinan and Qingdao, as well as Takei, First Secretary of the Embassy in Beiping, Nakayama, the consul in Zhangjiakou, and Fujii, the consul in Shanhaiguan, are all scheduled to come to Tianjin on the morning of the 17th. As for Ishimoto, the director of the South Manchuria Railway, and Sogō, the president of the China Development Company, they are scheduled to arrive in Tianjin on the morning of the 20th to attend Kawagoe's North China consular conference and provide economic development data. (16th)

Song Zheyuan Returns to Beiping from Baoding, Inspecting Various Counties to Rectify Officialdom and Combining Facts with the National Assembly Election in Hebei and Chahar 65

Beiping Correspondence: Song Zheyuan, Chairman of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee, left Beiping for Baoding on the 4th of this month and inspected Renqiu and other places. He finally returned to Beiping by special train at 6 p.m. on the 15th. All heads of agencies went to the station to greet him. That evening, Song summoned the leaders of various agencies at his private residence in Wuyiku, inquiring about military and political affairs. Zhang Zizhong and Chen Juesheng also came to Beiping from Tianjin on the 16th to pay their respects and report on everything. According to Song, the course of this trip was roughly as follows: "The Hebei Provincial Security Office held a security conference this time. All counties considered the situation, and the county magistrate, the head of the public security bureau, or the deputy commander of the security brigade attended in Baoding. More than 100 people attended. The meeting was scheduled to end on the 4th, and everyone should return. Because it was not easy to gather, I stayed for another half day after arriving in Baoding on the evening of the 4th. On the morning of the 5th, I invited them to give a speech. The content of the speech was published in a booklet. The most important thing is to strictly prohibit opium. Because the ban on opium must start from the fundamental prohibition of planting. In the past, due to incorrect policies, it was not possible to thoroughly ban it. Therefore, all opium investigation offices in various counties have been cancelled. In the future, anyone who opens a lamp (for opium smoking) or sells opium will be treated as a bandit once caught. Then I inspected the troops stationed in Baoding and tested the officers' academic and martial arts skills. Later, I went to Renqiu to watch officers above the company commander level practice shooting. Because in the army, if the officers are proficient in academic subjects, the soldiers will also be proficient. This decision to go on inspection was originally intended to visit many counties, but after arriving in Renqiu, it rained heavily that night, and it rained again the next day, so I didn't go to many places. The purpose of the inspection is to rectify officialdom and clear up backlogged cases. Renqiu County alone has many backlogged cases. Among them, there is a deserter detained by a certain army whose name has not yet been decided. Such cases are common in various counties. Generally, after the troops stationed in an area leave, no one cares about the prisoners. The cost of prisoner rations in Hebei Province alone reaches more than two million yuan a year. Clearing up backlogged cases is very important. An order has been issued to all counties in the province to clear up all military cases from now on. In addition, the Cangxian County Magistrate was punished for dereliction of duty, and the Jinghai and Yanshan County Magistrates were punished for not reporting bandits and beautifying peace. The Daxing County Magistrate was punished for violating orders and apportioning money. At the same time, the previous order was reiterated that from the 25th year (of the Republic), no apportionment is absolutely allowed. During this time in Baoding, it was decided to absolutely and thoroughly implement two things this year: one is to reorganize the additional taxes in the province. In the future, the additional tax on land tax shall not exceed four yuan at most. The other is to rectify the people's militia security team. The first step is to eliminate the bandits and people who disturb the people in the team. The second step is to train and organize them. After these two steps are done, then stipulate the methods for the security team to go to the countryside to support themselves. Now, everything that is being done is aimed at relieving the suffering of the people. There has always been a gap between officials and the people. I believe that whatever the people need, we must actively promote it. Whatever the people consider painful, we must quickly relieve it. Only in this way can we eliminate the gap. The harvest in Hebei Province this year, as it stands now, can reach 70-80%. If it rains again, we can expect a full harvest." In addition to the above remarks, Mr. Song also answered several questions from reporters, which are recorded below: (1) The recent small disturbances in Suiyuan are caused by Mongolian bandits and puppet troops on the border of Chahar and Suiyuan. But these troops are all a rabble, and those who help them dare not say so clearly. Moreover, the Suiyuan army has a very strong combat capability, and the bandits are not worth a single blow. I believe this matter will not lead to any major changes. (2) Whether the Japanese ambassador to China came to the north this time to be responsible for contacting the development of the North China economy was not reported in advance. (3) There is no definite date for Wang Kemin's arrival in the north. The matter of taking office as the chairman of the Economic Committee has not been discussed recently. The issue of Sino-Japanese economic cooperation in North China has not been negotiated recently either. (4) The construction of the Cangshi Road is the request of others. I intend to accept local investment. Under the principle of fairness and mutual benefit, it is also possible to purchase its materials. However, if it is still insisted on priority, it will be very difficult. (5) Regarding the election of delegates to the National Assembly in Hebei Province, we should take into account the facts and not affect the overall situation as a prerequisite. It is not yet certain whether it will be circled and sent by the central government in the future. (16th)

Puppet Troops Active in Northern Chahar; De Wang to Organize Security Team into a Division; Zhang Haipeng's Troops Flee from Rehe to Baochang; Japanese Automobile Company Manipulates Commerce 66

Zhangjiakou Correspondence: The puppet troops in northern Chahar are actively expanding. According to transportation sources, De Wang is still in Jiabusi (i.e., Jiapu Temple). He is currently gathering the security teams of the six counties in northern Chahar, gathering them in Jiapu Temple, and organizing them into a division, totaling more than 3,000 people. The guns and uniforms are also quite neat, and he is asking a certain party to issue military pay and train them. However, a certain party is only responsible for training and does not provide military pay, which is still raised by De Wang himself. Yuan Dupeng holds an important position in the expansion of the division. Yuan previously served as the captain of the security team in northern Chahar. He is extremely sinister. All merchants in northern Chahar know his name. His mother is Korean, and his father is Chinese. He has a lot of contact with a certain party. Now, all the bandits in northern Chahar feel that they are oppressed internally by a certain party and have no possibility of development externally, and they all intend to turn against them.

The bandit army of Zhang Haipeng's department, with more than 2,000 people, has already arrived in Baochang County in northern Chahar from Rehe and is still continuing to move westward. It will join forces with the bandit gangs of Wang Ying and Wang Daoyi in Shangdu to attack Suiyuan. The military supplies are completely supplied by a certain party. In addition, 500 people from the puppet army of Li Shouxin's department in Zhangbei have arrived in the Kangbao area of Shangdu. De Wang held an important meeting with 11 puppet military and political figures such as Bao Yueqing in Jiabusi. One theory is to join forces with Wang Ying, Li Shouxin, Wang Daoyi, and Zhang Haipeng to attack Suiyuan. Another theory is to take considerable contact with the Suiyuan army to solve the bandit army. It is still waiting for confirmation. Suo Wang still lives in Zhangbei, and there is no news of leaving Zhangbei recently.

After the puppet army occupied northern Chahar, except for the Dabe, Wenlin, and Donglu three automobile companies operated by certain nationals, which can pass freely, the other automobiles have been successively shut down. The transportation of goods is also contracted by these three companies. Recently, the organization of the Great Mongolian Company has been restored to manipulate the general hub of commerce in northern Chahar. All goods dumped by a certain party in northern Chahar are transported to northern Chahar by the Great Mongolian Company from the eastern provinces via Rehe. The national goods sold in northern Chahar are also rented by the Great Mongolian Company in Zhangjiakou with automobiles with the flags of a certain country inserted on them and transported to the north. The commerce operated by the Chinese in northern Chahar is now in a state of extreme panic. (14th)

Huai Bei Salt Industry Bankrupt; Salt Merchants Petition to the Ministry of Finance; Shanghai Banking Circle Agrees to Loan 3 Million; Contract to Be Signed After Salt Price Balance 67

Haizhou Correspondence: Northern Huai is a salt-producing area, and Banpu is the administrative area in the center of Northern Huai. Auditors, salt fields, and merchants are all concentrated here. In recent years, due to the impact of the current situation and natural disasters, salt production has been reduced, and transportation and sales have been sluggish. At the national level, the tax revenue has decreased. At the salt field and merchant level, not only is life in a state of panic, but the salt worker fees are also difficult to maintain. Salt workers want to produce but have no one to rely on, and they cry bitterly all day long. In particular, the drop in salt prices exceeds the drop rate of ordinary agricultural products. Salt is a daily necessity, and its cost of assets and labor are the same as agricultural affairs. The rise and fall of market prices should also be at the same rate. Now, the market prices of ordinary agricultural products, such as rice and wheat, have fallen by 30% to 35% compared with five years ago, and it is generally recognized that there is an urgent need for relief. However, the drop rate of salt prices has exceeded 50%, which is contrary to the normal degree of economic curves. Recently, the cost of salt production has exceeded the market price significantly. If the salt price drops and the cost is reduced accordingly, it is still possible to offset each other. However, the government sends a field affairs officer to each number of salt fields, and raises the treatment of laborers, salt worker rations, and labor costs, etc., which increase year by year. Since the construction of Guantuo in the 22nd year, salt production must be carried out in a limited period of time. Each number also increases the cost of lightering salt, signing seats, sacks, hooking, and carrying, etc., by more than fifty yuan, so that the cost of each number of salt is more than 270 yuan. Compared with the current market price, each number of salt loses fifty or sixty yuan. Most of the salt fields and merchants have no ability to produce salt. In addition, the banking circle has stopped issuing loans, so all the salt merchants in Northern Huai are in a desperate situation. A petition group for increasing mortgage prices and borrowing money in Northern Huai was recently organized to petition to the Ministry of Finance and the Lianghuai Transportation Envoy's Office, and went to Shanghai to negotiate a loan. As a result, the Shanghai banking circle agreed to lend 3 million yuan. Petition representatives Qiu Menglin, Luo Fangbo, and Li Yangren, etc., returned from Shanghai to report the results of the petition and remove the salt affairs official Hong Man. The Preparatory Office of the Huai Bei Salt Industry Association was reorganized and formally elected members of the supervisory committee to establish a formal Salt Industry Association. The original representatives were still elected to go to Shanghai again to carry out the loan work. Soon Luo Fangbo returned from Shanghai to the association and reported that the loan of 3 million yuan had a definite grasp. This time, he returned to Pu on the order of the Shanghai banking circle, specializing in handling the formalities for balancing salt prices in the association. Once the handling is completed, he will go to Shanghai to handle the signing. The Salt Industry Association has properly balanced the salt prices in Northern Huai and submitted them to the Liang Huai Transportation Envoy's Office for review. Once approved, Luo will go to Shanghai again.

Songjiang 68

Expanding School Buildings in the County

Muyi County Middle School has developed greatly in recent years, but the school buildings are limited, and there is almost a problem of overcrowding. Xia Zhongfang, who lives next door to the school, is a famous doctor in the county and is very enthusiastic about education. He believes that the county middle school has made great achievements in cultivating young people, so he completely donated his own residence and newly built houses. After receiving the donation, the school not only published a thank-you notice in the newspaper to promote his benevolence, but also built dormitories and dining halls on the land donated by the Xia family, and demolished and rebuilt the auditorium to make it more spectacular.

On the morning of the 15th, he went to the bureau to take over and inspect the work, and summoned all the police officers to give a speech. He then announced the important personnel appointments. Suzhou 70

Cart Driver Mutual Assaults Lead to Fatal Incident

Wang Da, a resident of No. 13 Hongling Lane in Pingmen, Funing, made a living pulling rickshaws. At 4 pm on the 16th, near the Chanxing Temple Bridge on Hulong Street, he had a conflict with a fellow rickshaw driver over robbing business. He even assaulted Wang Da, who was seriously injured. The perpetrator saw that he had caused trouble and immediately slipped away. Wang Da still pulled the rickshaw with pain after being injured, but he collapsed in front of the Tianfu Tea House. The police station sent him to the County Hospital for treatment, but he died at the entrance of the hospital. His wife, Zhang, learned the details and asked the police district to arrest the murderer and investigate the case. The District Prosecutor's Office sent staff to inspect the scene at noon on the 17th, ordered the family to collect the body, and strictly arrested the murderer to bring him to justice.

Wuxi 71

Implementing the Police Management District System

Zhang Da, the Director of the Public Security Bureau of Wuxi County, officially took office on the 15th. All the staff in the bureau and the directors, inspectors, and officers of the nine branch bureaus and eight branch offices in the urban and rural areas must receive considerable training because this county has been designated by the Department of Civil Affairs to change to the police management district system. Except for Li Junjian, Min Junzhong, and Jin Wu, the other three were all replaced. This time, 36 police officers who graduated from the Provincial Police School were commissioned and arrived in Wuxi from the province the day before yesterday. After a rest, they went to various branch bureaus and offices to serve. In addition, 181 police officers also arrived in Wuxi from the province the day before yesterday and were sent to various bureaus and offices to work on the same day. Director Zhang originally intended to implement the police management district system in this county. All police officers in the branch bureaus and offices must pass the examination. The excellent ones will be sent to the province for training to transport the considerable knowledge of the liquid police management district system. Yesterday morning, he specially ordered the six branch bureaus in the urban area to transfer a part of the police to the bureau, and Director Zhang, together with the police supervisors of the Civil Affairs Department, examined the academic and martial arts skills and gave a speech to determine the selection and dismissal.

It was also reported that the new Director of the Public Security Bureau, Zhang Da, took office on the 15th, and on the 16th, he ordered the removal of the directors of the six branch bureaus in the urban area and the three branch bureaus in the rural area, and also replaced all the inspectors of the branch bureaus. 232 elderly police officers were laid off in the bureaus. 29 police officers and 184 trained police officers were sent by the Jiangsu Provincial Government to serve in the bureaus. The laid-off police officers were scheduled to take an examination on the 18th, and 181 were prepared for recruitment and transferred to the province for training. The police officers in the bureaus were very panicked when they heard this news. Suddenly, at about 10 pm last night, they all went on strike and decided to go to the county government to petition tomorrow (18th). Zhang Da immediately led more than 100 police officers to suppress the situation in various places after receiving the report.

Certain Nationals Buy Up Rice Bran

The rice bran of each rice mill has been sold to various counties in Jiangbei to be used as fertilizer and duck feed. This year, due to the bumper harvest in Jiangbei, the sales volume is very small, so each factory has a large stock. However, in the past few days, the price of bran has suddenly soared, rising by 3-4 cents per stone compared with usual. The reason is that certain nationals specially entrusted the Tianjin gang to buy it in Wuxi for oil extraction, so in the past few days, more than 10,000 dan of bran stored in each factory have been sold out.

Robbery Case Solved Quickly 72

The home of Wang Ruyuan, a grain merchant at No. 2 Lime Field in Beizhakou, Muyi, was robbed by five bandits at about 11 pm on the 15th, claiming to be delivering express mail to Suzhou. They robbed 943 yuan in paper money, 3 flower hairpins, 9 pieces of silverware, and 2 gold rings, totaling more than 1,000 yuan. It is now known that the public security authorities paid unusual attention to this case after it occurred. The perpetrator of this case was Yao Ayu, the shop assistant from Changchunyu Rice Shop under the Huinong Bridge. The rice shop was also opened by Wang Ruyuan. Ayu was a substitute worker of a certain person. Because he coveted the wealth of the shop owner, he gathered a group of accomplices, including Shen Hongsheng and Yin Zhongliang, and went to rob. The next day, Wang Bingsheng and Dai Quan, the detectives of the Public Security Bureau's Detective Team, captured Yao Ayu based on confidential reports. Then they captured the two criminals Shen and Yin, and arrested Shen's mother, Li, at No. 25 Xinfangs Community, and found the original stolen goods such as hairpins, paper money, and gold rings. They were all taken to the team and interrogated strictly. The criminals confessed to robbing Wang's house without any concealment. They were all handed over to the Public Security Bureau for review on the 17th.

Changzhou 73

600,000 Citizens Sworn in

The citizens of Wuyi County were ordered to complete the registration of the oath by the 15th of this month. Under the strict supervision of the county government, it has been able to end on schedule. County Magistrate Hou Houzong was eager to report, so he notified each district to report in the fastest way. The total number of registered citizens in the county is about 600,000. The county government immediately printed and distributed the citizen certificates according to the number of oath forms reported. However, the procedures such as filling in and stamping are time-consuming. Additional personnel were specially allocated to work overtime to rush the work, and it is expected to be completed within two weeks.

Director Shen Inspects the Sluice

Shen Baixian, Director of the Jiangsu Construction Department, believed that the Menghe Sluice project in Wujin was of great importance. He took a private car on the morning of the 16th and set off from Zhenjiang, arriving directly at Menghe Town. Zhenjiang 74

Cart Drivers and Dung Carriers on a Major Strike

The Zhenjiang County Government and the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau previously believed that most of the rickshaw drivers in the provincial capital were from other provinces, and there were people from all over the world, and there was no statistics. In order to facilitate investigation and maintain road administration, after formulating the ban rules, they presented them to the Construction Department for review and approval. The Provincial Government Committee approved them on January 31 of this year and allowed them to be implemented. After receiving the order, the county government decided to handle the registration of rickshaws in the provincial capital starting from April 30. However, very few people registered in accordance with the regulations by the deadline. The authorities believed that the matter was a pioneering undertaking, so they announced an extension of 20 days. However, it was still ineffective by the deadline. After extending the deadline to August 10, those who drove without a license would be punished in accordance with the regulations. However, most of the cart drivers still delayed registration. The county government detained a small number of cart drivers who had registered but not paid the license fee. The general cart drivers did not know the truth and disturbed each other. On the previous (14th) day, they gathered at the Chamber of Commerce to petition, but the result was not resolved. The authorities insisted on registering the cart affairs to collect manure, causing the problem of where to dump the chamber pots of each family. The streets and lanes were filled with manure and water, and the stench was overflowing. Pedestrians could not help but frown and cover their noses. By the morning of the 16th, the strike of rickshaw drivers and manure carriers was expanding. Although various institutions and organizations ran around to persuade them, it was still ineffective. On this day, Min Chunhua, the director of the General Labor Union, invited the cart driver masses to talk and promised to completely relieve the suffering of the workers and eliminate disputes. He immediately telephoned the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau to report the course of the conversation and asked the bureau to bail out the two cart drivers in custody. Director Chuan did not want the strike to expand, so he released them at any time. On the one hand, the General Labor Union held a meeting to discuss relevant measures, based on the principle of maintaining the government's prestige and relieving the suffering of the cart drivers. The cart drivers also claimed that they were good, but within an hour, more than 2,000 people suddenly carried their wives and children and paraded in formation, each holding red and green paper flags with petitions, and marched east from Yinshan Dou Street. At the same time, at each street and lane entrance, they would prevent those who carried manure from working. The stores announced their closure upon hearing the news. If there were those who did not agree, the cart driver's family would beg for food from them. The city appearance was chaotic for a while. In order to maintain order, the authorities dispatched a large number of unarmed soldiers and police to suppress the situation along the way. Fortunately, no accidents occurred. On the one hand, they advised the stores to operate as usual, and stopped the cart drivers from moving forward in a peaceful way. However, due to the large number of people, it was impossible to disperse them. The cart drivers arrived at the Provincial Government at about 10 o'clock and gathered in front of the hall without leaving. Director Chuan of the Public Security Bureau persuaded them in a tactful way and promised that the cart drivers would be allowed to operate as usual before the registration matter was resolved. The cart drivers were satisfied and dispersed, and the strike of cart drivers and manure carriers came to an end.

Bengbu 81

Actively Reorganizing Anfeng Pond

Anfeng Pond in Shouxian County, Anhui Province, was opened by Sun Shu'ao in the Han Dynasty, also known as Qisi Pond. The function of the pond is to divert water to irrigate the fields in Huainan. Historically, it was as important as the Jingqu in Shaanxi as an important irrigation project in our country. It has been dredged and treated in all dynasties until the end of the Qing Dynasty, so the water conservancy is still thin. Since the Republic of China, it has been out of repair for a long time, resulting in the siltation of the Piyuan and the interruption of the water source. When the water is small, it can only irrigate 12 miles outside the pond. When the water is large, it can only irrigate 18 miles. In dry years, the pond trough is silted up, and the fields are barren, resulting in a large reduction in the harvest. Since the National Economic Commission dredged the Jinghui and other canals, local people in Shouyi have repeatedly requested the association to restore Anfeng Pond to benefit the people's livelihood. Subsequently, the Huai River Guidance Committee sent technical personnel to conduct on-site surveys and establish an Anfeng Pond Reorganization Engineering Office to design the reorganization. The reorganization funds require 130,000 yuan. It is estimated that after the dredging project is completed, it can irrigate 200,000 mu of farmland. It is now heard that the National Economic Commission has allocated funds for handling, and the Huai River Guidance Committee is now actively engaged in dredging to promote reorganization.

Explanation of Chamber of Commerce Elections - Explanation of Doubts

The National Election General Affairs Office yesterday telegraphed the Shanghai Election Office, saying: (1) Shanghai Supervisor, Inquiries have been flooding in recently regarding doubts about Chamber of Commerce elections. To put it simply, there are four points: (1) How should store members of various trade associations be recorded in the group roster? (2) Who exercises the voting rights of the aforementioned members? (3) Does each store have one vote, or does each representative have one vote? (4) Do store members of the Chamber of Commerce have the right to nominate and elect? The explanations are as follows: (1) The store's brand name, the representative's name, age, place of origin, and the length of time they have been engaged in their occupation should be recorded. (2) In accordance with the Election Law and Article 24, Paragraph 2, the store is regarded as a trade association group member, and its representative is regarded as a member of that group. (3) Each representative only has one vote. (4) Store members of the Chamber of Commerce are permitted to have their member representatives have the right to vote, but not the right to nominate. This is hereby telegraphed to be followed and ordered to be obeyed by subordinates. National Election Office, Xian Yin. (2) Shanghai Representative Election Supervisor, It is reported that Wu Guozhen, the Mayor of Hankou, telegraphed to inquire about Article 18 of the Occupational Election section of Chapter 3 of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Election Law. The organs of the lowest-level group in a professional group are as follows: The Chamber of Commerce is the various trade associations to which it belongs. There is no provision for "store members." Can the aforementioned "store members" participate in the election and the nomination of candidates? If they can participate, in what way should they nominate candidates? Please provide separate instructions. It is found that Article 9 of the Chamber of Commerce Law stipulates: "Chamber of Commerce members can be divided into two types: 1. Association members, 2. Store members. The aforementioned members shall send representatives to attend the Chamber of Commerce, called member representatives." Article 14 of the same law stipulates, "Member representatives shall have the right to vote, the right to elect, and the right to be elected." That is, regardless of whether they are association representatives or store representatives, their rights and obligations are completely equal. Now Article 24 of the Election Law stipulates, "The election of National Assembly representatives shall be conducted by the members of the lowest-level group of each professional group." The regulations for the implementation stipulate, "The lower-level groups of the Chamber of Commerce are the various trade associations to which it belongs." As for store representatives whose businesses have fewer than seven members of the same trade and are unable to organize a trade association, and instead directly join the Chamber of Commerce, there is no clear provision on whether they have the right to participate in the Chamber of Commerce group election. It has now been decided by this office that they should be allowed to participate in the election in accordance with the National Assembly precedents. Since this matter concerns the interpretation of laws and regulations, in addition to replying by telegraph and issuing separate orders, Supervisor should be informed. National Assembly Representative Election Headquarters, Yan Yin.

This is addressed to the medical associations in various regions, from the Shanghai Medical Association."

The National Federation of Physicians has recently received letters and telegrams from medical associations in various regions claiming that there are doubts about the General Election Office's notice regarding the mixed election of Chinese and Western medicine practitioners. Yesterday, the Federation submitted a request to the General Election Office to clarify the nature of the Physicians Association and the National Physicians Association. The original text is excerpted below: "Regarding the request to immediately designate a legal group to comply with laws and regulations and benefit the electoral administration, the association previously stated that if the physicians in the category of physicians and pharmacists listed in Table 4 of this National Assembly Representative Election Law include both Chinese and Western medicine, difficulties will inevitably arise in the election. We have asked your office to explain or clearly delineate the quotas to provide relief and facilitate the process. However, according to reports, there is still a resolution to hold a mixed election. This association has repeatedly received letters from the majority of physicians associations in Shanghai, Zhenjiang, Wuxi, Hangxian, Wuxian, Minhou, Hankou, and other regions stating that the physicians associations in each region have applied for registration in accordance with the Public Associations Organization Law and have been established for many years. Subsequently, so-called National Physicians Associations have appeared in the same region. If these organizations are considered to be trade associations of the same nature as physicians associations, it would conflict with the purpose of the Public Associations Organization Law, which stipulates that there cannot be a second trade association of the same nature in the same region. The relevant authorities 'actually allow the existence of such organizations, which clearly demonstrates that they are not trade associations of the same nature.' If this election recognizes these National Physicians Associations as physician groups and gives them the same electoral qualifications, there will inevitably be two trade associations of the same nature competing in the same region. Considering the laws and regulations, there is a conflict. According to the facts, it is difficult to implement, etc.' After repeated consideration, this association is unable to resolve the issue. The only option is to submit a request to your office to clarify the nature of the Physicians Association and the National Physicians Association, and to immediately issue a clear order designating one as a legal group to comply with laws and regulations and benefit the electoral administration. This would be for the public good. Respectfully submitted to Jiang, Director of the National Assembly Representative Election Headquarters, and Chu, Deputy Director, by Xu Naili, Chairman of the National Federation of Physicians."

Postal Workers Union

Regarding the participation of the Postal Workers Union in the National Assembly elections, after the National Postal Workers General Union and local postal workers unions submitted requests, the National Assembly Representative Election Office and the Central People's Training Department consulted and reached a concrete solution. The Shanghai Election Supervisor yesterday received an instruction from the General Office, Min Zong Zi No. 33, which reads: "It is found that the National Postal Workers General Union, the National Postal Workers General Association, and local postal workers unions have jointly submitted requests to re-verify the quota of special representatives of the Workers Union. In addition, the Nanjing Postal Workers Union, the Hankou Postal Workers Union, the Shanghai Postal Workers Union, the Jiujiang Postal Workers Union, the Xiamen Postal Workers Union, and five other locations have successively submitted requests for approval to participate in the general industrial sector elections. Based on this, whether the National Postal Workers General Union, etc., are legally organized and established is not on file with this office. After writing to the Central People's Training Department to verify and respond, a re-examination will be conducted. We have now received a reply stating that the following four points have been decided regarding the issue of the Postal Workers Union's participation in the National Assembly representative elections: (1) All local postal workers unions that have been registered with the local senior party department and whose organization and organizational members are temporarily complying with the provisions of the Trade Union Law and its implementation regulations may participate in the representative elections in the local industrial sector. (2) All local postal workers unions that have previously been registered with the local senior party department but whose organization is not yet sound may temporarily comply with the Trade Union Law and its implementation regulations and immediately reorganize and rectify. Those who can complete the reorganization before the National Assembly elections may participate in the representative elections in the local industrial sector. (3) Local postal workers unions that have not previously been registered with the local senior party department, or have been registered with the local senior party department but whose organization is illegal and cannot be handled in accordance with item 2, are not allowed to participate in the election. (4) The organization of the National Postal Workers General Union, the National Postal Workers General Association, and the provincial and municipal postal workers associations has no legal basis and is not allowed to participate in the election. These replies have been reviewed and approved. In addition to notifying the election supervisors of all provinces and cities to comply, the National Postal Workers General Union and the National Postal Workers General Association will be notified, and replies will be sent and orders issued. The supervisor is hereby ordered to comply, investigate whether the local postal workers union is a legally organized and directly provide instructions, and report the handling situation for future reference. This is of utmost importance. This order, etc." It is also heard that the Shanghai Election Supervisor, after receiving the order, has presented a report to the General Office to comply, etc.

Sincere Expression from the Financial Sector: Rural Loans. Restore the Rural Economy, Safeguard Industrial and Commercial Development, Reducing Interest Rates to Rescue Industry and Commerce is Not a Fundamental Solution. 83

The industrial and commercial sectors of this city, in view of the economic downturn and sluggish business, have requested the Ministry of Finance to order various banks and money shops to reduce loan interest rates in order to reduce costs and promote development. After receiving the request, the Ministry of Finance, in order to safeguard industry and commerce, specifically instructed the Shanghai Banking and Money Industry Associations to study and present methods for reducing loan interest rates for review and approval in order to provide relief. After receiving the order, the Banking and Money Industry Associations organized a group meeting. After several discussions, they gathered various opinions and submitted them to the Ministry for review and approval. A New News Agency reporter learned from the financial sector that reducing loan interest rates is, in fact, fraught with difficulties and may not be implemented. It is said that our country is an agricultural nation, with farmers accounting for more than 80% of the population. Therefore, most of the various goods produced by factories rely on farmers for purchase. The industrial and commercial sectors only act as intermediaries, taking a small profit. In recent years, due to the global economic recession, coupled with repeated disasters, the rural economy of our country is on the verge of bankruptcy. The purchasing power of farmers has decreased, and industry and commerce have also declined as a result. Therefore, the prosperity or decline of the rural economy is closely related to the prosperity or decline of industry and commerce. After research by experts, it is generally believed that developing industry and commerce should first focus on cultivating the countryside. As for reducing loan interest rates to rescue industry and commerce, it is not a fundamental solution. Reducing loan interest rates must first reduce deposit interest rates. Otherwise, the financial sector will inevitably have no business to operate. If deposit interest rates are reduced, the result may be that people's cash will be absorbed by foreign banks, and there is a risk that domestic funds will flee. Therefore, in order to avoid the occurrence of this situation, various banks and money shops are now actively engaged in rural loans. The results achieved can directly gradually restore the rural economy and indirectly safeguard the development of industry and commerce.
