US Increases Tax on Chinese Wine - Chinese Wine to Disappear - Chinese Merchants Suffer Annual Loss of US$500,000 to $600,000 - Additional Taxes Added Besides Consolidated Tax and Stamp Duty 88

After the United States lifted the alcohol ban in 1934, Congress promulgated the Liquor Tax Law, which requires all types of alcohol to pay a consolidated tax and stamp duty. Alcohol dealers must pay a license tax. Chinese medicinal wines were widely sold in the United States during the alcohol ban period. Recently, the United States mainland recognized that Chinese medicinal wines with an alcohol content of 24% or more will be treated as strong alcohol from June 1 this year. In addition to paying a consolidated tax, stamp duty, and license tax, various surcharges must also be paid (resulting in a sharp increase in the burden, making it impossible to compete with other wines and leading to their disappearance from the US market. Details are recorded below:

Types of Wine Sold to the US

The types of Chinese wine sold in the US market include Wujiapi wine, Bai Nuo wine, black Da wine, Laiyang wine, Winter Melon wine, Papaya wine, Kumquat wine, Shi Guogong Sanzheng wine, Rose wine, Baili wine, Sanbian wine, Ginseng and Velvet Antler wine, Gecko wine, Dragon and Tiger wine, Baisui wine, Chicken Claw wine, Tiger Bone Country wine, Wei wine, Yinchen wine, Orange Blossom wine, etc. For example, Wujiapi wine sells for only 50 cents per bottle in Shanghai, while it currently sells for US$2.80 in the US. During the prohibition period, strong and weak wines were both banned. However, medicinal wines only needed to obtain an import license to be imported in a steady stream without restrictions. Therefore, in the past, except for strong and weak wines, imports were relatively reduced, and medicinal wines had a very wide market. Since the lifting of the ban in 1934, the number of Chinese wine exports has been even greater.

Taxation

The types of taxes paid by Chinese wine exported to the US are: (1) The consolidated tax is paid by the manufacturer or importer. For strong alcohol, it is US$2 per standard gallon. For weak wine, it is US$0.10 per gallon for alcohol content below 14%, US$0.20 per gallon for alcohol content above 14%, and US$0.40 per gallon for alcohol content above 20%. For alcohol content above 24%, it is taxed as strong alcohol. (2) Stamp duty: when retailing, strong alcohol requires a stamp of US$0.01 on the bottle. (3) License tax: (A) Wholesalers pay an annual business tax of US$100. (B) Retailers pay an annual business tax of US$25. (C) Manufacturers pay an annual business tax of US$200. For annual production below 500 barrels, it is US$100.

Imposition of Miscellaneous Taxes

Since the lifting of the alcohol ban, all Chinese wines, whether strong or weak, have been taxed according to regulations and have been imported in a steady stream. However, medicinal wines were considered to be medicinal materials rather than beverages according to the US Customs interpretation and were exempt from all consolidated taxes, stamp duties, and license taxes in addition to the import tax, which greatly benefited overseas Chinese merchants. From June 1 this year, the United States mainland considers Chinese medicinal wines to be beverages in fact, even though they are medicinal wines according to the customs regulations. In addition to paying consolidated taxes, stamp duties, and license taxes, surcharges must also be paid in the same way as strong and weak alcohol. The amount is very large, making it impossible for Chinese wines to compete with other wines in the future, leading to their disappearance. The future is extremely pessimistic. Chinese merchants will suffer an annual loss of US$500,000 to US$600,000.

Page 13

Yangtze River Water-Land Passenger Joint Transport - Tripartite Agreement Already Signed - Implemented on the 21st of This Month 89

The state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, together with the Shanghai-Nanjing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway and the Jiangnan Railway, will operate joint water-land passenger transport on the Yangtze River. After a long period of discussion, the three parties agreed on joint ticket methods and submitted them to the Ministry of Transportation for approval. A contract was signed by the three parties and will be implemented from the 21st of this month. The details are as follows:

Process of Agreement

Regarding the joint passenger transport between the Yangtze River and Shanghai, and the detailed rules for joint tickets, Mr. Hu Quansheng, the head of the passenger transport division of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, has been in contact with the railway bureau and has submitted a request to the Ministry of Transportation for verification. As the various parties involved in the railway have reviewed the established methods and found them appropriate, Mr. Xiao Weiguo from the two railway bureaus and Mr. Zhou Xiansong from the Jiangnan Railway were dispatched yesterday to sign a trial contract together with Mr. Zeng Guangqing, the business director of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company.

Date of Implementation

The tripartite contract stipulates that it will be implemented starting from August 21st. A trial run will be conducted for half a year, expiring on February 21st of next year. If the results are deemed excellent during the trial period, all parties willing to continue may do so. As the implementation date is approaching, all water-land joint tickets have been printed and are sold by the ticket sales division of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. The price of the joint tickets is a quarter cheaper than the usual segmented transfers. The Jiangnan Railway has also dispatched a special train that can go directly from Wuhu to Zhenjiang, and the tracks have been connected.

Locations of Joint Transport

The locations for the Yangtze River water-land joint transport have been agreed upon. For the land route, the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway runs from Shanghai North Station, through Suzhou, Wuxi, Wujin, and Zhenjiang West Station, to Yaohuamen. For the Jiangnan Railway, it is from Yaohuamen, Zhonghua Gate, Dangtu, Xuancheng East Station, to Wuhu. For the water route, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's ships will take passengers from Wuhu, through Datong, Anqing, Jiujiang, Wuxue, to Hankou. Passengers traveling from Shanghai to Wuhu can take the train at North Station at 7:00 AM and arrive at around 5:00 PM that afternoon, which is 29 hours shorter than taking a Yangtze River boat.

Fixed Ticket Prices

The water-land train and boat joint tickets from Shanghai by train, transferring to the Jiangnan Railway, and then by China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's ships via the Wuhu waterway, have been priced segment by segment. However, to provide preferential treatment to passengers, there is a 25% discount for first and second class and an 11% discount for third and fourth class. The ticket prices are as follows:

Shanghai-Nanjing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Ticket Price List

Jiangnan Railway Ticket Price List

Wang Junsheng Speaks of Continued Burial After Autumn Cools, Requiring Considerable Expenses, Hoping for Assistance from Benevolent People - In four locations including Wujiang and Jiaxing, coffins are scattered across the fields. Those without descendants have been exposed for more than a year, and their bones are exposed with no one to manage them. According to investigations, there are as many as tens of thousands of such exposed bones. Over the years, Mr. Wang Yiting of Shanghai has commissioned Mr. Wang Junsheng of the Pushan Villa to raise large sums of money to bury ownerless exposed bones in areas such as Wujiang, Zhenze, Pingwang, Bei*, Jiaxing, Puyuan, Nanxun, Wangjiangjing, and Wangdian. Over the years, more than 80,000 bones have been buried, bringing peace to the deceased and greatly benefiting charity and hygiene. People have praised this endlessly. According to Mr. Wang, there are still 60,000 to 70,000 exposed bones in Wujiang, Jiaxing, and other places that have not been fully buried, which makes him uneasy. However, to bury them one by one would require considerable expense. He is currently discussing the funding with various benevolent people, hoping to continue the work after the autumn cools and begin working, hoping for generous help to accomplish this task, so that the exposed bones can be put to rest in peace, a great merit.

Real Estate Bank - Difficult to Realize 97

Financial Circles Express Opinions - No Confidence in Preparation

Ta Kung Pao reports that, in view of the decline of the real estate industry, the Ministry of Finance specially ordered Song Ziliang of the China Construction Bank to be responsible for preparing for the establishment of a real estate mortgage bank in order to facilitate the flow of funds and adjust finance. The work has been temporarily suspended because the Real Estate Compulsory Execution Law has not yet been formally promulgated. The reporter specially asked the financial circles yesterday about the establishment of a real estate mortgage bank and the future environment. According to the opinions expressed, they are quite important. The following is a record of the conversation. In recent years, due to the extreme exhaustion of the social economy, no one in this city has inquired about real estate. For example, many urban houses or residences are empty. All real estate merchants have suffered heavy losses and are eager to seek a way out. The establishment of a real estate mortgage bank cannot be flexibly rotated with only several million in capital. Once real estate merchants mortgage a large number of properties to the bank at the same time, the bank will be unable to cope, and business will be extremely dangerous. The Ministry of Finance plans to allocate half of the bank's 5 million capital and raise the other half from various banks. Currently, the various banks are wary of joining the capital due to the above-mentioned difficulties. Therefore, although the preparatory office of the real estate bank has been established, there is still no confidence in the actual preparation, it is said.

Detailed Account of Xue Jiasheng's Escape from Danger: Bandits Planned for Ten Months Before Taking Action; Backstage Boss Provided Advance of Over Two Thousand Three Hundred Gold Coins 110

Xue Jiasheng, the third son of the deceased wealthy Jiangyin paint merchant Xue Baorun, was kidnapped from his residence on the afternoon of the first of this month. Fully Armed

Obtain Tens of Thousands of Dollars

In ransom money. Next, Pu Yaozhang, Zhang Ruifa, Sun Yanan, and Chen Dongsheng were questioned. All four denied participating in the kidnapping. Female Tea Server from Tianyunlou Sues Hotel Manager for Refusal of Indecent Assault, Resulting in Overnight Confinement, Followed by Forcible Seizure of Gold Jewelry as Payment for Room 116

Zhou Gengsheng, 39 years old, a native of Zhejiang, is the owner and manager of the Shangxi Hotel at number 11 Pingan Lane, Fuzhou Road. Wang Xingbao (21 years old), a female tea server from Tianyunlou at Wing On Company from Luodian, reported to the Laozha police station the other day that around 11 PM on the 14th, Zhou Gengsheng sent two apprentices to Tianyunlou to ask her to go to Shangxi to talk. She immediately went and was led to room number 18 upstairs. Zhou was already waiting there. The apprentices who led her in exited. Zhou then tried to take off her clothes. She sternly refused. Zhou left in anger and locked the door, confining her in the room until around 9 AM. Zhou returned to the room and demanded a room fee of five jiao. Because Zhou had someone call her over, and it was not her intention to come, she refused to pay. Zhou then claimed that she owed two yuan and five jiao in previous room fees. Since she had never owed any money, she denied it. Zhou then instructed her to take off her two gold earrings and a gold ring to pawn them for cash to pay the debt. A and B, two workers, accompanied her to Hongxing Pawnshop on Hubei Road to pawn them. The police sent Chinese and foreign detectives to the Shangxi Hotel to arrest Zhou Gengsheng, who was escorted to the First Criminal Court of the Special District yesterday morning, where Judge Feng Shide presided over the hearing. First, police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated the previous events and prosecuted Zhou for obstructing freedom under Article 302 of the criminal code, and stated that the stolen goods have not yet been recovered, and requested a postponement for further hearing. Zhou Gengsheng, the defendant, confessed that Wang Xingbao often brought men to open rooms, owing two yuan, ninety-two cents in room fees, which could be verified in the accounts. The other night, when Wang came, Zhou asked for previous debts, and Wang took her gold rings and pawned them herself. Zhou did not take off her clothes, and did not lock her in the room. Wang Xingbao confessed that she and Zhou had a previous arrangement. He sent someone the other night to call her to play, and after she went, he asked her not to go home, and tried to take off her clothes. After she refused, he locked her in the room. The next morning Zhou came and forcibly seized her gold rings and pawned them to pay the debt, but she had never owed any room fees. Judge Feng verified the confessions and ordered Zhou Gengsheng to pay a five hundred yuan bail and postponed the hearing to next Friday.

Six Months Imprisonment Suspended for Two Years

Guo Hongbin, a native of Shandong, lives at number 17 Huasheng Lane, Huasheng Road. He is a martial artist in the Shaolin Martial Arts Troupe of the Dajing class at Wing On Company. He has two sons and one baby girl, named Qiaoying, who is only four months old. She recently suffered from diarrhea. On the morning of the 8th of this month, around 5:00 AM, without his wife Gong's consent, Guo secretly fed the girl opium ash. The poison took effect, and she died at 9:00 PM. When I ordered him to move, the defendant threw lime at my face. Fortunately, I had on a peaked cap, which prevented serious eye injury. Bailiff Sun Qingshan stepped forward to negotiate, but the defendant threw lime again and took out an axe. I then turned and went outside to call the police, so I did not see him砍傷. Seizing an opportunity, he fled to the police station to report and was arrested. Pregnant Woman Aborts After Taking Medicine

Du Youming, a native of Funing, 31 years old, lives on the east side of Tanzi Bay Temple, where he works as a night soil collector. His wife, Mrs. Yang, 29 years old, is currently six months pregnant. After taking the medicine, Mrs. Yang suffered abdominal pain like a knife. Her illness did not subside, and instead, she aborted her baby, and her condition was very critical. Destroying a Trunk of Clothes with Acid 138

Unable to Murder His Paramour; Ruan Suisheng Sent to Court for Questioning

Lin Yufeng, a young woman from Jiangsu residing at No. 12, Baxian Cun, Route du Père Robert, in the French Concession, is 23 years old. Her husband, Chen Bingsheng, was involved in the kidnapping case of foundry owner Xiang Yixing and was arrested by the Public Security Bureau and sentenced by the First Special Court to imprisonment. While he appeals, Lin Yufeng has no one to rely on and has cut off her life support. A friend introduced Lin to Ruan Suisheng (also known as Shouzheng, 30 years old, from Shaoxing, residing in Xiangshun Lane, Cashi Road, French Concession), a clerk at the Xu Zhengda Copper and Tin Shop on Beijing Road, who is now her paramour. They have been cohabitating for four months. Initially, Ruan agreed to pay Lin Yufeng a monthly living allowance of 37 yuan. He provided the full amount for the first two months. In the last two months, Ruan told Lin that he was experiencing financial difficulties and could not afford to pay, suggesting that Lin pawn all her clothing for money. Lin refused and reproached Ruan. Ruan felt ashamed and resentful. Some days ago, he secretly obtained nitric acid and, taking advantage of Lin Yufeng's absence, opened her leather trunk and poured the acid on dozens of her valuable cotton, silk, and padded garments, worth 500 to 600 yuan, causing the clothes to be completely ruined. He then disappeared and no longer stayed overnight at Lin's place. On the 14th of this month, Lin Yufeng opened the trunk to take out clothes and discovered that the inside was wet and dripping, and the clothes were all ruined. Knowing that Ruan was responsible, she reported the incident to the French Police the next day. On the 16th, Detective Jiang Zhongjia went to Ruan's residence and arrested him. Yesterday, he was sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special Court. Judge Zhang Minsheng interrogated him. Attorney Fei Xizhen from the Police Department explained the case and requested a postponement of the investigation before filing charges. The court examined the warrant and questioned the defendant, who admitted the crime. The court adjourned the hearing to investigate further. The defendant was returned to custody. The plaintiff, Lin Yufeng, told others that the defendant poured the acid during the period from the 9th to the 14th of this month.

Dai Jixian's "Interpretation of the Civil Procedure Law" Reissued 144

The Civil Procedure Law is essential reading for legal practitioners. Schools emphasize the Civil Procedure Law course because all legal acts in society are related to civil law, and the procedure for protecting private rights lies in the Civil Procedure Law. However, the articles are complex and difficult to remember. To fully understand and apply it, it is necessary to rely on a interpretation of the Civil Procedure Law that fully explains and applies it. After the jurist Dai Jixian published his "Interpretation of the New Civil Procedure Law," it was well-received by legal professionals. In addition to interpreting each legal article, its content connects and applies all articles and related laws, making it convenient and practical. The first batch has sold out, and the second batch has now been published and is still being sold at the Shanghai Bar Association.

The Shanghai Film Industry (Continued) (Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce - 34) 150

(3) Business Methods of Films

The business methods of films can be broadly divided into the following three types:

(1) Revenue Sharing - That is, the ticket revenue from the opening of the film is split between the film company and the theater. However, the percentages vary. The common method is 50% for the film company and 50% for the theater. In addition, there are splits of 40/60, 30/70, or more for the company and less for the theater, or vice versa, depending on the circumstances. Currently, most theaters in Shanghai, both Chinese and foreign, adopt this method.

(2) Film Rental - The theater rents the film from the film company, setting a rental price for a fixed period. The theater shows the film on its own, and the company only collects rent and does not share the revenue. The rental price depends on the situation in each port and the length of time. For example, the price for renting a re-run film should be cheaper. This method is mostly used for good films because the theater is certain that the film will be a box office success. Therefore, it sets a rental price in advance, and the income should be higher than revenue sharing. On the company side, it can also avoid the trouble of revenue sharing.

(3) Purchasing Exclusive Screening Rights - That is, the theater or intermediate manager purchases a copy from the company, setting a price and region. Within that region, the company or other distributors may not screen the same film. This method is used most by distributors in Southeast Asia. For example, Nan Yi Company in Shanghai purchased the exclusive screening rights for Chaplin's "Modern Times." The price has no fixed standard.

(4) The Current Situation of Public Distribution Centers for Various Films

(1) The Current Situation of Various Film Companies - The number of existing companies has decreased significantly compared to before. This is because technological advances and the increase in the audience's level have made it impossible for those who produce crude and insipid works to gain a foothold, as well as the government's strict prohibition of speculation. According to a survey conducted by Lianhua Company, there are currently eleven companies in Shanghai, of which only seven actually produce films. The list is as follows:

Masseuse's Client Commits Theft: Swallows Gold Ring, Discovered After Doctor's Examination; Masseuse Recounts Theft 151

Xu Zijun, a Ningbo native residing at No. 10 Wanxiang Lane, Aerjin Road, aged 29, went to the Jianermei Massage Parlor at No. 861 North Sichuan Road at around 1 PM the day before yesterday for a bath. He was attended to and massaged by Wang Xiangyun (also known as Wang Zhang, aged 20), a woman from Huzhou. Shortly after Ms. Wang went to another room, she suddenly heard a sound coming from a box in the room. She rushed back and discovered that two silver coins and a key ring were missing from a small tin box placed on the massage table. At the time, because Xu Zijun was a customer, and the loss was minimal, she did not make an issue of it. Unexpectedly, around 4 PM, when Xu was getting ready to leave, Ms. Wang shook his hand and suddenly discovered that a gold ring she was wearing on her finger had vanished. At this point, Ms. Wang began to suspect that Xu was not a good person, so she instructed a tea server, Weng Ali, to chase after him and question him. An argument ensued between them on the road. Policeman No. 2379 arrived and took Xu into custody at the Hongkou Police Station. Two silver coins and a key ring were found on Xu, but the gold ring was nowhere to be found despite a thorough search. The police suspected that Xu had swallowed the ring, so they sent him to the Public Concession Hospital. After an examination by the doctor, it was confirmed that the gold ring was indeed in his stomach. Xu was admitted to the hospital for treatment. Yesterday morning, the police's lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, filed a lawsuit against Xu in the Special First Court according to the law, and recounted the details of the case, requesting a postponement. Additionally, the masseuse Wang Zhang recounted the above situation. Judge Ye Shengchao reviewed the testimony and ordered the case to be postponed for a hearing this Friday.

Husband and Wife Commit Suicide in Wu Palace Inn: Deceased Named Wang Tiansheng, From Anhui; Reason: Despair Due to Business Failure 152

On the afternoon of the 13th of this month, a young man and woman checked into the Wu Palace Inn at the intersection of Fujian Road and Fuzhou Road, booking room number 429 for their stay. The man claimed to be Wang Tiansheng, aged 27, and the woman was his wife, aged 25, both from Anhui province. They had been staying in the room for several days, rarely venturing out, and nothing seemed amiss. Unexpectedly, around 6:50 PM yesterday (the 17th), tea servers suddenly heard faint groaning sounds coming from the room. They knocked and received no response, which aroused suspicion. They forced the door open and entered, finding the two lying stiffly on the bed, pale and on the verge of death. Alarmed, they immediately reported to the police station, who dispatched a vehicle to rush them to the hospital for treatment. It was determined that they had committed suicide by poisoning. However, due to the severity of the poisoning, they both died shortly after. A suicide note was found beside them, addressed to the manager of the Wu Palace Inn. It stated that they had failed in business in Hangzhou and had lost all hope, so they had decided to commit suicide together. They also stated that the money owed for the room could be covered by selling their luggage. The police are currently trying to locate their family members.

Sports News

World Games Closing Ceremony Grand Spectacle, Solemn and Weighty Ritual 154

Special Correspondent of the Central News Agency, Berlin, 17th Broadcasting: The Eleventh Olympiad has come to a successful conclusion since its opening on August 1st. The closing ceremony was held at 8:45 PM on the 16th. German Head of State Hitler arrived at the venue at 5 PM and did not leave until the ceremony was over. The ceremony was solemn and simple. Representatives of each country entered the venue one after another, holding their national flags (one representative per country), in the same order as the opening ceremony, except that Germany was last this time. After the representatives of the 51 countries stood in their positions, the President of the Assembly, Lado, delivered a brief closing speech. Two thousand German students sang the assembly song, and several female students in uniform hung wreaths on the flagpole, fired thirteen cannons, lowered the assembly flag, rang the assembly bell, and extinguished the assembly flame. Representatives of each country left the venue with their flags, and five strong men carried the assembly flag, while eight men in white uniforms escorted the flag to the podium. The Mayor of Los Angeles, America, handed the flag over to the Mayor of Berlin for safekeeping. The mayors of both cities gave brief speeches. The chairman also announced that the first session was held in Greece, the last session in Los Angeles, this session in Berlin, and the next session will be held in Japan. The national flags of Greece, Germany and Japan were raised on the flagpole, and then lowered one after another. The audience at the venue sang the German national anthem and cheered for Hitler. The solemn and grand closing ceremony was thus completed.

Reuters Berlin, 16th: Nearly 100,000 people attended tonight's closing ceremony of the Olympic Games, including Hitler. More than a dozen arc lights illuminated the entire venue. The Olympic flame, which had been burning since the opening, was extinguished. The assembly flag was gradually lowered. In silence, the public gave the Olympic salute. After a minute of silence, a loudspeaker announced, "I now command the youth of the world to go to Tokyo." This was followed by a high-pitched singing of the German national anthem, the National Socialist Party song, and the Olympic song. The conference then closed.

Lado's Closing Remarks

Havas Berlin, 16th: The Eleventh Olympic Games, since its opening on the first of this month, half a month has passed in an instant. All events have been completed. Until 9 PM tonight, Count de Lairado, the chairman of the International Olympic Committee representing Belgium, announced the closing and said, "On behalf of the International Olympic Committee, I would like to express our sincere gratitude to the German head of state Hitler, the German people, and the Berlin authorities, the organizers of the games with enthusiastic emotions. I hereby declare that the Eleventh Olympic Games has come to an end, and I invite the youth of all countries to gather in Tokyo for the Twelfth Olympic Games in 1940. It is hoped that the Olympic Games can be held on time in a pleasant and peaceful atmosphere. The Olympic flame will be passed down from generation to generation and will never be extinguished, and the will of all mankind will be influenced by the Olympic spirit, becoming more noble, pure and brave."

One of the Most Memorable Scenes

(National Maritime News Agency) Berlin, August 16: Today, at the World Games venue, where the atmosphere was tense and emotions were high, outstanding athletes from 52 countries officially bid farewell to each other. This solemn closing ceremony is undoubtedly one of the most memorable scenes in modern sports history. The venue was packed to the brim, and the seats reserved for journalists were also occupied by many nobles and guests from various countries. At the same time, the streets of Berlin were filled with enthusiastic people, the number of whom was impossible to calculate. The total number of guests and tourists who came from abroad over the weekend to witness the spectacle of the World Games was over one million. Before dawn, the World Games venue was already full, because those who had obtained tickets were still afraid that they would not be able to get a seat, so they entered the venue early. The order began at 2:30, first with equestrian performances and the awarding of yesterday's prizes. Prime Minister Hitler entered the venue at 3:00 PM sharp, and everyone stood up to pay their respects and sing the German national anthem.

The Five-Ring Flag Slowly Descends

When all the competitions were over, it was 7:30 PM, and the closing ceremony was held. The athletes from all countries entered the venue in uniform, very solemn and tidy, no less than on the day of the opening two weeks ago. All the athletes lined up and passed the viewing platform first, then gathered in the center of the sports field. When all the athletes were in place, the Chairman of the World Games Committee, Lardur, addressed the crowd. At the same time, the speech by Count Coubertin, the restorer of the World Games, was also published on the bulletin board, stating that "The World Games torch can illuminate the future, so that there can be more brave, pure and progressive human beings." When a horn sounded, the heroes of each country handed their national flags back to the referees in front of the viewing platform. The national flags were then tied with laurel wreaths. As the music was melodious and the cannons sounded, the five-ring World Games flag slowly descended, and the World Games torch was gradually extinguished. As the military band played a farewell song, the national flags of the fifty-two countries in the venue also slowly descended. The applause in the venue was deafening. Everyone who participated in the closing ceremony had a very deep and solemn impression.

When asked about his feelings about the China-England match, he replied that he had never set foot in Europe, and he did not know the strength of the European teams. The reporter informed him that the fatigue of the journey had a great impact on his strength. Mr. Li said that fortunately, there were more than ten days for our people to rest, so it was not too late.

Miss Yang Xiuqiong and Miss Li Sen had dinner at the Nanjing Hotel on the evening of the 26th. More than a dozen people were sitting at the same table, including a receptionist and translator, and Ms. Wang Nanxi, a female student studying in Germany. Yang and Li both had smiles on their faces and ate very hard.

Since the schedule of the World Games football match was arranged, after China's first match against England, the reception office of the Chinese Students Association in Germany immediately handled the purchase of tickets. It is known that more than 350 students have registered to buy tickets, which shows their enthusiasm. It is heard that the ticket prices are divided into three types: 4 marks (with seats), 2 marks and 1 mark (without seats).

Education News

City Education Bureau Issues Order to All Schools: Prohibiting Female Teachers from Perming Hair and Applying Cosmetics, Emphasizing that Teachers Should Lead by Example and Enhance the Effectiveness of Moral Education 165

The Shanghai City Education Bureau issued an instruction to all levels of schools under its jurisdiction, stating: "According to a report submitted by the Shanghai Primary School Teachers' Association, the purpose of the New Life Movement is to train the public to develop clean and simple habits and cultivate the spirit of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame. Although the specifics are minor, the effect is significant. Once advocated, it is promoted nationwide. Various organs in the city have repeatedly received orders from higher authorities, instructing them on the steps to take. Female students in various schools have been prohibited from various bad habits such as perming hair and applying cosmetics, and considerable results have been achieved. Recently, it has been observed that female teachers in various schools, who hold teaching positions and are regarded as role models, often have not eliminated various bad habits such as applying cosmetics and perming hair. It is inappropriate for them to serve society and educate children in this way. In recent years, international trade has seen women's cosmetics expenses as a major import item. With the country's affairs in such a state, how can we bear to engage in such time-consuming and money-wasting activities? The association feels deeply concerned and dares to request that your bureau issue an order to all female teachers in various schools to comply. As the ancients said, 'Please start with me.' Hopefully, the future of the New Life Movement will be promoted and developed through the efforts of women, and the future of education will advance boundlessly through the rectification of female teachers. Based on the above, it is found that the bad habits of female students in various schools, such as applying cosmetics and perming their hair, have already been strictly prohibited by the bureau. Now that female teachers in various schools are regarded as role models, they should lead by example and eliminate various bad habits such as applying cosmetics and perming their hair to enhance the effectiveness of moral education. Based on the previous report, all female teachers in various schools are hereby ordered to comply. This order is hereby issued."

Finance: October Contracts Hit the Market, Bidding Price Initially High, Then Flat - Market to Remain Closed for Another Week 177

Because of the sweltering autumn heat, the Gold Market announced yesterday that it would continue to be closed for another week in the afternoon. The situation was uncertain during the half-day session, but the overall trend remained stable due to the Central Bank's acceptance of cash. The morning session opened with overseas silver markets in London unchanged and the US closed. Monte Carlo forward silver prices remained unchanged or fell by as much as 5 points. Exchange rates were flat. London spot gold was unchanged. The Central Bank's listed price was flat for both the UK and the US. The Customs Gold Unit was unchanged. The standard bidding price was still listed at 1124.9 yuan. Unofficial pre-market trading opened at around 28 yuan. Hengchangyong entered the market to buy, leading to a higher opening. If swap transactions were added, it would only be 4 jiao. After the opening, the market fell as those taking advantage of the high prices to sell surged, and short sellers increased their positions. Supply in the market exceeded demand, causing a decline. However, large investors took advantage of the low prices to limit their purchases, which helped maintain the market. Floating positions were then advanced. HSBC's listed price was flat for both the UK and the US, and the silver balancing tax was unchanged, having little impact. However, the market was pulled up by the rumor that the Central Bank would open the spot market at a flat price. It then moved sideways. By noon, it had returned to stability. Yesterday's swap transactions were offered by long positions at 2 yuan to 2.6 yuan. Here is a record of the half-day market situation:

The morning opening was 1128.8 yuan, up 2.4 yuan from the previous swap. Yiyu Shengyuan Yongyuan Mao Yongda Decheng Yongde Yicheng Ding Kang Huixiang all sold off. It fell back to 7.3 yuan. Qiafeng Yongshen Dayong Futai Yong Futai Heng Qingfa Yong successively purchased strips. HSBC's exchange rates for both the UK and the US were unchanged, and the silver balancing tax was also flat, with no significant impact in the middle. It was only pulled up by the rumor that the Central Bank would open the spot market at a flat price. However, there was much sideways movement. By the time the market closed at noon, it had risen to 1128.3 yuan.

The closing price was still listed at the Central Bank's standard bidding price of 1124.9 yuan. In terms of the closing price, it rose by more than 3 yuan. September contracts were all traded at 1127 yuan. The ledger for this month was 1124 yuan, September was 1126 yuan, and October was 1128 yuan. The additional water for the morning settlement was 1124 yuan. Pure gold was increased by 8 yuan to 1136.8 yuan. The spot market was stable, but the additional water was slightly cheaper due to swap transactions. Tianjin goods were increased by 13.5 yuan. The buying price for refined gold was 13 yuan, and the selling price was 15.5 yuan. In the September-October swap, Tongfengheng offered Shengyuanyong 35 strips at 2.1 yuan. Yuanmaoyong offered Shengyuanyong 28 strips at 2.2 yuan. Daheng offered 7 strips, Dachangxiang 14 strips, and Yuanmaoyong 63 strips, all taken in by Qianchangxiang at 2.1 yuan. Daheng offered 14 strips and Yuxinxiang 70 strips, which were taken in by Futaiheng at 2 yuan. As for the spot market swapping into September, long positions offered about 5 jiao, which was due to the Central Bank's continued acceptance of cash.

Trading in the market was normal. In summary, Futaiheng, Chunyuan, Yongda, Fengheng, Qingfayong, Hengchangyong, Shendayong, Xiangfeng, Qiafengyong, and Dacheng were among the buyers. Shengyuanyong, Hengyu, Ding, Yiyu, Wanxing, Yicheng, and Yongde were among the sellers.

The half-day market situation was unstable. The opening was 1128.8 yuan, and the noon closing was 1128.3 yuan. The highest was 1128.8 yuan, and the lowest was 1127.3 yuan, with a fluctuation of 1.5 yuan. The result was an increase of 1.9 yuan compared to the previous swap. Yesterday, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange restored full-day four-session trading, and the market was quite active. After several days of sideways movement, it suddenly turned firm, mostly induced by swap transactions in the supply and demand of chips. For many days, those who had been selling the 10th suddenly covered their positions, which was particularly noteworthy. There were no good news in the environment. The Gui incident remained as it was, and the situation in the East was still quite tense. Even Wang Kemin's trip to the north had nothing to do with the entry and exit. However, those who were generally nervous believed that there was a good impression with 96, so those who were generally accustomed to raising the price of 96 believed that the time had come and suddenly raised the price by 4-5 jiao. The future cannot be viewed with optimism just because of the increase. Yesterday's situation was that the opening in the morning was still virtual in the hearts of the traders. Types Wuding were still a little less than 1 jiao to 1.5 jiao. Type C of this month was still sluggish due to the outflow of spot goods in the 4th. Starting from the far term, there were still more people covering their positions. The 10th also had purchases, and the market price gradually turned firm. The closing market was revitalized, and the trend was unanimously higher. The 4th and 11th continued to sell, and Type B was still weak and powerless. The rest generally rose by 1 jiao to 1.5 jiao. The opening in the afternoon was extremely firm, and the market price soared, gradually becoming stronger. Although the 4th and 11th continued to sell, the 10th, 54th, and scattered retail investors absorbed quite fiercely. The market price unanimously rose again by 1-2 jiao to 4.5 jiao. The closing was as firm as ever, and the rising trend was still strong. Most bonds rose by another 3-4 jiao. The 96 also gradually rose in rumors and misinformation, rising 4-5 jiao throughout the day. Uniformity and each government bond rose by 3-4 jiao to 9 jiao. The total number of transactions was 8,635,000 yuan. Here is a table comparing the results of the rises and falls (unit: yuan, transaction unit: 100 yuan):

Yarn and Cotton: Little Liquidation of Cotton Contracts, this Month Up 1.1 Yuan 180

--New Cotton Buying Interest Also Strong--

--Distant Months Trade Above 1 Yuan--

Spot month cotton prices opened lower, following declining US cotton prices to 5 pounds. This resulted in a reduction of the value of cotton Robbies by one-half. Spot cotton prices generally increased by 2 to 3 jiao. Tensions in the market increased, owing to unfavorable conditions, including overcast skies and continuous torrential rains and flooding in the Subei region, damaging crops. Buyer activity increased as a result. After the first session, prices climbed progressively higher. All months of Spot cotton saw increases of 3, 4, and 5 jiao respectively compared to previous closing prices, while August alone increased by 1.1 jiao. Reported sales included 3400 bales from Jifeng, 1300 bales from Yuda, 1800 bales from Gengfeng, 1700 bales from Lianchang, 1700 bales from Shenji, 4000 bales from Changfeng, 1400 bales from Shengyuan, 1600 bales from Xincheng, and 5100 bales from Zhaoye. Buyers included Hengyi, who purchased 2100 bales, and Yuhang, who purchased 1800 bales, Mingde purchased 5500 bales, Hexing 1300 bales, Changyu 1000 bales, Renfeng 1000 bales, Yicheng 1900 bales, Runhang 1500 bales, Xiecheng 1900 bales, Fuhang 4100 bales, Yongda 1000 bales, and Yihang 1100 bales. Highs and lows in half-day trading are listed below.

Spot Cotton Merchants Stay Cautious

Current cotton consumption is moderate, with factories adopting a cautiously observant attitude, resulting in scant trading activity.

Yarn Prices Boosted by Cotton, Spot Yarn Market Highly Active, Jincheng Yarn Opens at 2000 Bales 181

The yarn market is trending firm and the overall situation is stable. Yarn sales are brisk, and market sentiment is optimistic. Lack of new selling is tightening up order books. Furthermore, poor weather has caused cotton prices to rise, which in turn has led to a further strengthening of the interconnected yarn market. Yong’an Mill released 2000 bales of Jincheng 20s yarn, priced between 214.5 and 216 yuan, for delivery in November and December, and reported that all had been sold.

Mingde Buys Up Balances of Spot Yarn

The spot yarn market opened with prices showing listless and sluggish activity, partly due to overseas yarn and cotton markets being flat and without energy, contributing to poor market sentiment. Unexpectedly, after the second session, it was reported that yarn sales were strong. Mingde again began taking up balances of contracts, which strengthened the market. All months rose from 8 or 9 jiao to 1.2 or 3 yuan respectively, while Gengfeng and Changfeng closed out numerous long positions, contributing significantly to market activity. Upon the third closing, short positions in the market were covered up. Spot yarn prices closed with all months increasing from 5, 7, and 8 jiao to 1 yuan, in comparison to previous closing prices. Reported sales included 200 bales from Dafu, 950 bales from Tongji, 1300 bales from Gengfeng, 500 bales from Changji, 500 bales from Ruida, 550 bales from Shenji, 2200 bales from Changfeng, 1100 bales from Runhang, and 700 bales from Shengyuan. Buyers included Juxing, who purchased 1700 bales, Mingde purchased 3200 bales, Xingchang purchased 700 bales, Shenkang purchased 400 bales, Weiyu purchased 500 bales, Dachangcheng purchased 600 bales, Dachang purchased 500 bales, and Yongda purchased 450 bales. Highs and lows for the half-day market trading sessions are listed below.

Yarn and Cotton Deliveries Are Forthcoming This Month

Standard yarn and cotton deliveries for this month at the Chinese Merchants Yarn and Cotton Exchange are scheduled to take place on the 29th. Trading for this month will be suspended for three days on the 26th, 27th, and 28th, and the market will be closed on the delivery day.

Cotton-Growing Regions Still Worry About Lack of Rain, Development of Indian Cotton Still Pending 182

Following initial sharp falls early in the week in line with US cotton reports, prices have recovered slightly on the back of bargain-hunting by merchants and European exporters. Consumer demand from India and overseas remains subdued, and near-term trading remains constrained by manipulator activity. Crop yields remain a concern due to lack of rain in some areas. Overall, further developments remain to be seen. Weekly figures for this past week are appended below. (Units in thousands of bales)

July US Cotton Statistics Report (Units in Thousands) 183

Three-ply Yarn and Cotton Yarn All See Rebound 184

Osaka Telegram, July 7th: Futures yarn rose 7.7 jiao to 1.3 yuan. Near-month is 107.4 yuan, distant-month is 100.5 jiao. Futures cotton rose 1.5 to 4.5 fen. Near-month is 65.4 yuan, distant-month is 60.95 yuan.

Overseas Cotton Market Sees More Declines Than Rises 185

American cotton opening: Liverpool news was unfavorable. Foreign merchants sold shipments to Bombay and Liverpool. Local bulls also closed out positions. All months fell 5 to 12 points. Currently, the market's focus is on changes in the international political situation and the increase in Southern hedging. Dealers bought on dips. New Orleans also purchased here, but sellers sold on rallies. Subsequently, consumption increased, the West continued to be dry, and cotton quality declined, leading to a rebound. As a result, spot prices fell 5 points, futures fell 5 points to rose 1 point. English cotton spot prices fell 17 points, futures fell 14 points. Indian cotton was initially firm due to purchases by European exporters but then fell due to large-scale selling by operators. It then rebounded due to purchases by speculators. Overall, Pingguoer fell 1.25 rupees, Aola fell 4 rupees, and Bainanxi fell 3.75 rupees. Original telegram recorded on the left. (Telegram of the 15th)

Piece Goods: Smuggled Goods Decrease; Cotton Cloth Sales to the North See Renewed Increase; Japanese Fine Cloth Lacks New Transactions Across All Regions; Overseas Sales Are Quite Good, So There Is No Fear of Oversupply 186

Yesterday's cotton cloth market: Unbleached and printed piece goods mostly maintained the previous weekend's prices. Eastern fine cloth and fine twill experienced a decrease in new transactions across all regions because dye factories had already prepared sufficient quantities of white fine cloth and fine twill for this month. Therefore, there was a wait-and-see attitude towards fine cloth and fine twill, with no immediate plans, resulting in a sharp decline in the momentum of Eastern fine cloth and fine twill. However, Japanese factories did not feel any oversupply because sales to the South Seas were quite good. But the market had already become flat and fatigued because of it. Yesterday, the market price for each piece of fine cloth, fine twill, and grey cloth from various dealers decreased slightly, about 2.5 fen per piece. The Tianjin syndicate in the Northern route, which had been quiet for a long time, saw a sudden increase in shipments of Shanghai goods due to the decrease in smuggled goods since last week. They continuously purchased over 200 boxes of Qingfeng Factory's heavy crepe, Jianmei呢, Mingxing呢, and other goods, as well as over 300 pieces of this factory's 16-pound coarse cloth, light-pound coarse cloth, and group twill. Purchases of Southern route Sichuan and Hunan printed velvet and white velvet were also strong. However, Guizhou, Yunnan, Guangdong, and Guangxi were all extremely sluggish. Guangdong is about to implement currency reform. After the situation stabilizes and financial adjustments are made, there may be a large number of purchases.

Grains: Strong Bullish Sentiment; Futures Flour Rises Universally 187

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, all months showed a universal upward trend. The quoted price of foreign wheat had little fluctuation. The opening price of the current month was initially stable because the appetite of Northern buyers had turned sluggish. But because market sentiment was good, and short covering emerged, it rose from 9 fen to 9.75 li. Therefore, the opening prices for September and subsequent months were all raised by 2 fen due to the bullish sentiment around them. Currently, market sentiment is rising unabated, partly driven by Japanese purchases of wheat, and partly by the promotion of increased agricultural production. Moreover, public and private propaganda suggests that domestic prices are much cheaper compared to foreign countries, leading to upward sentiment with almost no setbacks in recent months. After one round of trading, the price of the current month rose again due to heavy short covering, while the rest generally hovered around. Observing future trends, it is feared that due to wheat exports, it will be difficult to see an easing of prices.

Both Futures and Spot Wheat Rise by Five or Six Fen 188

Yesterday in the futures wheat market, after the morning opening, each month presented an image of initial stability followed by brisk trading. The opening price of the current month, with little fluctuation in foreign wheat, remained at 4.967 yuan. However, when trading extended to September, market sentiment soared because the government paid attention to food supplies, and warehouses in various places had to be prepared. The opening price immediately rose by 3 to 4 fen. After one round of trading, the situation for the current month also tightened, and the highest price once broke through 5.02 yuan. Trading for other months was brisk, and prices stabilized. The future situation will depend on whether the export issue can be resolved, before the market can stabilize. In the spot wheat market, prices rose again by 5 fen due to customer buybacks and good factory appetite. The opening price for Linghuaiguan, Zhangbaling, and Yaowan wheat was 5.05 yuan, Liuhe wheat was 4.55 yuan, the secondary grade was 4.8 jiao, Jiangxi wheat was 8.78 yuan, Quanjiao wheat was 5 yuan, and the settlement was 4.95 yuan. Jiangxinzhou wheat was 4.95 yuan, Puzhen wheat was 4.9 jiao, and the settlement was 4.856 yuan, Taicang wheat was 4.81 yuan, Huaian wheat was 5 yuan, and the settlement was 4.95 yuan, Wuhu wheat was 4.87 yuan. Fuxin bought 7,000 bags, and Fufeng bought 1,000 bags. As for the Japanese side, there are no movements reported.

Foreign-origin Sesame: The Association Already Has Futures Trading; The Highest Price Has Reached 12.7 Jiao 189

For standard foreign-origin sesame, the exchange does not conduct auctions because there are still about two months before the new crop arrives. However, the miscellaneous grains syndicate already has forward trading in the association's market. The opening price was 11.5 yuan the week before. Recently, with inquiries from foreign merchants (namely Germany and Italy), the market has been exceptionally tight. It was heard that the price had already risen to 12.6 yuan the day before yesterday. Yesterday, it initially tightened to 12.65 yuan, and finally reached as high as 12.7 yuan, with a situation where buyers could not cover their positions. Recently, China's agricultural exports have seen expansion. In the midst of an economic recession, there is a possibility of reversal.

The Rising Trend of Ke Xian Rice Continues Unabated 190

Yesterday's Ke Xian rice market situation: although arrivals were strong, with 6,000 to 7,000 bags arriving at the port daily, sales were even more active, with daily sales of over 10,000 bags. Yesterday, local inland buyers were even more greedy, and there were also inquiries from the Northern syndicate. Moreover, due to reports that the authorities, in view of this year's bumper harvest, advocated raising agricultural prices to help rural areas, on the one hand expediting storage in warehouses throughout the country, and on the other hand finding other outlets, market sentiment became even more optimistic. Through smooth trading, the market price immediately jumped by 2 to 3 jiao, and market sentiment continued to be optimistic. Yesterday, the entire city opened with 4,810 bags of Jiangxi rice, 710 bags of Wentai rice, 2,500 bags of Hankou new unpolished rice, 780 bags of Jiangbei rice, and 1,500 bags of Dajiao rice. Purchasing appetite was not very strong.

White Rice Is Slow-Moving, Yin Yuan Rice Is Still Selling Well 191

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the total source of goods from various syndicates was on the 15th and 16th, with a total of over 3,000 shi. Sales in the local market of this kind became less urgent. Qingdao syndicate bought more than 400 bags. Therefore, although the market situation was considered settled, the situation appeared to be weakening. The prices of both thick and thin japonica rice were unchanged. Duyangjian rice was similar. Yin Yuan rice was selling steadily. A total of more than 1,000 shi arrived in Dongxin, sales were slightly less than before, and prices remained steady.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, very few goods arrived in the port from Hexia. Sales of white japonica rice on the 11th and 12th were sluggish, and Yin Yuan rice retail sales were still active. Yang Du Bu Ke Jian rice was normal, and thin rice was scarce. The price of high-quality white japonica rice was stable, and the secondary grade was tight. Yang Du Bu Ke Jian rice saw a slight increase of a few fen, and thin rice prices did not change. Yin Yuan rice was also tight by a few fen. Slightly more Dongxin japonica rice arrived, and sales were mediocre, with stable prices.

Silk and Tea: Lu Factory Products Are Uniquely Strong Due to Purchases by Users 192

The silk market in this port is still driven by strong buying interest from users, especially for Shandong yellow and white factory silk and Sichuan Yang return silk. In the past two days, a total of 62 boxes of the above-mentioned silk were sold, with prices remaining as firm as usual. Yesterday, Yokohama silk prices increased slightly by 32 yuan. Foreign merchants are still in the process of inspecting silk for export, and after the implementation of mandatory inspection in this port, the trading procedures for export silk products have not yet been unified (silk manufacturers and exporters all hold different opinions regarding the improvement of procedures). Therefore, export silk transactions are inevitably affected to some extent.

Zhenmei Green Tea Trading Is Quiet 193

Yesterday's tea market was still trending downwards. Arrivals of Zhenmei green tea from dealers and the removal of bud tea are still sluggish. Common dealer goods from areas such as Sexi and Siyuan were purchased by Xiehe, Yihe, Tongfu, and Du De companies, but because prices from Morocco were tight, Chinese merchants were weak-hearted. The market had already opened at around 70 yuan, and Su'an and Shexian goods fell to 57 or 58 yuan, a drop of another 2 or 3 yuan from before. Needle eyebrow pearl tea and other items also saw some sales, but Qining black tea was still sluggish yesterday, and the market situation was gradually declining.

According to a report from the Tea Industry Association, the green tea market returned to a static state yesterday, and Zhenmei transactions were sparse. Guanxi Baitu Company, which sold well last week, also showed signs of slackness. Only the 500+ amount of Zhenmei from Central Anhui, which was agreed upon last Saturday at a price of 65 to 70 yuan, was officially transacted yesterday. Jinlong, a major Ping Shui tea dealer, continued to import Tianxiang and Nenyu. In addition, Xiehe handled 870 boxes of colored pearl tea at a price of 56 to 58 yuan.

Dried and Preserved Goods: Orchid Bamboo Branches Experience a Shortage, Rising Three Yuan; Although the Quality of Orchid Seeds Is Good, Improvement Is Still Needed to Remove Sand and Debris 194

Since the mid-market decline of orchid bamboo branches, the price of Zhangzhou products has not been able to keep up and has recently risen again. Therefore, the source is scarce, and the trend is gradually turning around. Yesterday, it was heard that higher-priced goods had already risen by about 1 yuan. However, calculating based on the production price, it is still difficult to break even. Therefore, dealers still have some inventory and are waiting to see, and have not yet disposed of it. If later batches arrive in small quantities, the market may have to tighten further.

A small number of orchid seeds from the previous initial batches were offered at very high prices. Recently, as regular grade goods have been released into the market, the quantity has gradually increased. Yesterday, it was heard that hundreds and dozens of boxes had been offered, which was 3 to 4 yuan less than the previous round. The subsequent price drop is already close to 10 yuan. It has been observed that the quality of this local product is quite good, not only is it yellow, bright, and fragrant, but the texture is also relatively dry. However, it seems that it is not clean enough, which is a defect. Operators should improve this and remove the sand and debris in order to expand sales.

Sugar Market: Cantonese Refined White Sugar Up by Two Jiao, Domestic Green and Red Sugar Prices Remain Firm 195

Yesterday, the market saw little change, with few transactions. The guild set the price for No. 4 refined white sugar spot at 21.85 yuan, but no deal was made. Re-export goods were priced at 6.8 yuan. Eastern white sugar remained soft, with No. 4 spot at 21.5 yuan, and re-export goods down by a fraction at 6.5 yuan. A deal was made for No. 8 spot YJ mark at 21.12 yuan, and some deals were even made at a slightly lower price. Otherwise, there were few fluctuations. Domestic green and red sugar sales have been quiet recently, and trading companies have reduced their activity. The market is showing signs of softening, but prices in various production areas remain firm. According to a telegram from Guangzhou yesterday, Diao Qing sugar is priced at 10.8 yuan, and adding all external fees makes it difficult to profit.

The joint company held its first tender of Cantonese sugar for the week yesterday. The total quota was 12,644 bags. The prices for goods that arrived earlier remained the same. However, the refined white sugar produced by the Shunde factory was of better quality, and the tender price was raised by one jiao. 3,805 bags of "Five Rams" coarse white sugar from Shunde factory were sold at 21.6 yuan, and another 280 bags from the City New Factory were sold at 21.4 yuan, and 350 bags from Quxi Factory were sold at 20.9 yuan, and 90 bags of City Center sand white were sold at 19.3 yuan, totaling 4,525 bags.

Spring and Autumn

Opening Remarks 196

— (Skinny Wren)

Although I have never been to Guangdong, this vibrant cradle of revolution has long left a deep impression on my heart. The deepest impression, in particular, is the Guangzhou Uprising on the 29th day of the third month of the Xinhai year, which carved a bloody path for the revolutionary cause. Seventy-two people shed their blood, lost their heads, and generously sacrificed themselves. At the time, I sang for them, cried for them, and grew weary with sorrow for them. For more than twenty years, what has been constantly on my mind is the Huanghuagang, where those seventy-two martyrs lie in eternal rest; and because of Huanghuagang, I am reminded of Guangdong, the sacred place that initiated the revolution.

This summer, when Chen Bonan mobilized his troops and stirred up trouble, with swords drawn and bows stretched, I was apprehensive, deeply fearing that the seventy-two martyrs who sacrificed themselves without any rights would not even be able to rest in peace under Huanghuagang. Fortunately, the generals of Guangdong all understood the greater good and opposed the civil war. On the banks of Yue Wang Terrace, the bright breeze and clear moon reappeared, allowing Guangdong, which had been outwardly united but inwardly divided for the past seven years, to return from the hands of a tyrant to the banner of the central government. Rejoicing in the accomplishment of unification and the hope for the country, I created a special Guangdong section.

A Revolutionary Pioneer of Guangdong 197

— Ziwei

A guest who knows anecdotes about the uprising in eastern Guangdong told me about Mr. Yu Yuzhi's past support for the revolution.

Mr. Yu was a native of Taishan in Guangdong. His family was wealthy and ran a silver shop in Hong Kong. He was generous and liked to make friends. He was fluent in dialects, proficient in foreign languages, and possessed foresight from a young age. Seeing that powerful neighbors were watching like tigers, the Chinese people were in a state of slumber, the Manchu barbarians were in power, and the court was in disarray, Mr. Yu was deeply concerned. When Premier Sun Yat-sen passed through Hong Kong to promote the revolution, they became friends. He followed Premier Sun on travels between Nanyang and Singapore, and often interacted with veteran party members such as Chen Shaobai, Li Jitang, Yun Lie, Hu Zhantang, Feng Ziyou, and Xie Yingbo. At that time, the Qing court was strictly arresting party members, and Mr. Yu hid himself in business, remaining unknown to the public. Therefore, he secretly shouldered the responsibility of relaying messages, ensuring smooth communication, and his contributions in providing financial assistance to party members in need were particularly outstanding. After the Xinhai Revolution, he raised a large sum of money to assist Premier Sun, ensuring a source of funds and preventing shortages. However, Mr. Yu's family also declined. When Li Yutang was the head of the finance department, Mr. Yu was appointed as the head of the finance department by Mr. Hu Zhantang, but he ultimately declined the appointment, because Li was already in that position and it was not appropriate to take his place. He only recommended his nephew Chengqing to serve as the head of the treasury for more than ten years. When Premier Sun was stationed in Guangdong, Mr. Yu submitted a memorial offering suggestions on how to connect with Hong Kong merchants to provide assistance. He was invited to adopt the suggestions and sent Mr. Sun Zhesheng as a representative, carrying a handwritten letter and other documents, to the Tianxiang Foreign Firm in Hong Kong. Accompanied by Mr. Yu, he met with Liu, Wei, and other Hong Kong gentlemen to discuss cooperation, and the matter was successfully concluded. In the twelfth year of the Republic, Premier Sun established his government in the Southwest and was stationed at the Henan Cement Factory, gathering righteous troops from various provinces to plan the suppression of rebels. At that time, Mr. Yu was staying in Tianjin and immediately commissioned Comrade Yang Huiji to go south to offer suggestions, which were again approved by Premier Sun, who immediately appointed Mr. Yu as a member of the Central Finance Committee, but Mr. Yu declined due to illness. In recent years, he has been engaged in business, but has encountered frequent setbacks. Now, as an elderly man of sixty-eight, he is still running around in Shanghai, seeking a small profit to make a living. He has six sons. The eldest is employed by Taikoo Dockyard in Hong Kong, the third and fourth are employed by Texaco Oil Company in Hong Kong, the fifth lives at sea and runs the Dahua Lee Yeast business, and the youngest is still studying. Mr. Yu does not admire wealth or seek fame. He does not rely on his younger generation for support. His successful retirement is also commendable.

Guangzhou's Teahouses 198

— Sheli

The people of Guangzhou's addiction to tea is probably the greatest in China.

Early in the morning, they rush to the teahouse. At the entrance of the teahouse, there is always a newspaper stand selling all kinds of newspapers. These newspaper stands rarely sell them; they are almost always rented to teahouse patrons to take to the teahouse to read. The rental price is five copper coins per copy. Some more refined teahouse patrons throw down five copper coins, take a newspaper, and head to the teahouse, ready to while away the morning.

The size and number of Guangzhou's teahouses are also probably the greatest in China. Almost every bustling street has a large teahouse, decorated very luxuriously and cleanly, with many female waitresses. Some customers drink tea, read the newspaper, and flirt with the waitresses, appearing extremely leisurely amidst their busy lives. This kind of leisurely scene can only be seen in Guangzhou's teahouses.

Running back and forth in the teahouse are vendors selling all kinds of dim sum. The number of dim sum items is also unmatched elsewhere. The plates are especially small. One bun is also on one plate, and one piece of cake is also on one plate. Sometimes these plates fill an entire table, but your stomach is still not full.

Elsewhere, tea is always brewed in teapots, but in Guangzhou teahouses, it is all served in gaiwans, with a small cup, and you pour it yourself. This often causes those not used to it to spill water all over the table.

Huanghuagang Seventy-Two Martyrs Cemetery 199

Guangzhou's Summer Resorts 200

— Fangzong

Guangdong, which has just stabilized, is located in the southernmost part of China, close to the tropics, and the climate is usually very hot. But the hot south does not lack summer resorts. There are four places in the suburbs of Guangzhou. These four places are now bustling and prosperous, and do not change their normal state due to the tense situation. Now I will introduce these four places as follows:

(1) Huangpodong: Huangpodong is very close to Guangzhou, it can be said to be within the scope of the city. People who go there for summer can go early and return late. There are clear streams, shady trees, rugged rocks, and wildflowers everywhere. It is like a peach blossom paradise. Moreover, you can boat and swim in the cool streams. Therefore, young men and women, as well as small clerks from agencies and banks, love to go there to enjoy themselves to the fullest for a day, and because the journey is relatively short, the cost is extremely low.

(2) Conghua Hot Springs: Conghua Hot Springs, since the prominent figures of the party-state have been intent on operating it, are famous in Baiyue. And Mr. Hu Zhantang went there repeatedly to recuperate and discuss the current situation before his death, which made it even more famous throughout the country. From Guangzhou to Conghua, take the Conghua Highway bus, which only takes one hour. There are green mountains and clear waters, and the construction is very modern. The flying springs and waterfalls hanging high are even more magnificent. Villas of important people are everywhere, and selling snacks, raw fruits, soda, and paper is available everywhere. This is a paradise for important people and civil servants to play.

(3) Qingyuan Gorge: Qingyuan Gorge is farther away from Guangzhou, so people who go there must stay for a few days, or spend the entire summer there. And the scenery there is quiet, majestic, and like a fairyland. Taking a ship from the mouth of the Beijiang River, the mountains on both sides are verdant and the green shade covers the sky. It is a cool world, and waterfalls and flying springs are everywhere. The strange rocks are rugged and extremely dangerous, which is unmatched elsewhere. And there are also famous scenic spots such as Feixia Cave, Taihe Cave, Convent, and Xiashan Ancient Temple. Since the beginning of summer, it has become the world of wealthy merchants, tycoons, young masters and young ladies.

(4) Luofu Mountain: Boluo Luofu Mountain, also because of Mr. Hu Zhantang's repeated visits, is as well-known as West Lake in Hangzhou. There is a bus from Guangzhou to Luofu, so transportation is very convenient. The scenery of Luofu is very majestic, with more than 500 peaks on the entire mountain, of which the Elder Peak and Jade Maiden Peak are the most famous. The ancient Daron has Chongxu Temple, Baihedong Temple, Huanglong Temple and other Taoist temples. You cannot browse all over it without playing there for a month or two. This year, construction is advancing rapidly, with parks and hydroelectric power plants, so foreign summer vacationers take Luofu as their destination.

Moonlight Night in the South 201

— (Huang Kewei)

The moonlit night in the South is like a beautiful prose poem, a peach-colored musical score; its melody contains gentle tones, and its scenery is full of quiet flavor, enough to make people love and be intoxicated!

The dark green shallow edges, the flowing water floats curvingly over the broad leaves, like a few strands of silver snakes; the water ferry hits the smooth green stones, and pops out a uniform tone, like the soft breathing of a girl. The wind blowing from the beach is salty, shaking the long whiskers of the palm trees, and from time to time there are a few water birds that break through the bright silver waves and fly towards the bright moon, leaving a loud cry in the bright blue night sky.

Lying quietly under the coconut grove, whistling softly, the moon is hanging diagonally on the treetop, and the light like water leaks through the sparse thorns, as if sprinkling a handful of colored glaze pieces, brightly, spreading on the pine needle woven grass, the deep blue sea, in the silver whirlpool, flying fish float happily.

Gently strumming the erhu, singing a song of the loner, longing for the wandering girl who roams on the journey for life: she has a tan healthy skin color, she has dark eyeballs like purple grapes, she has soft hair like sea waves, she has the enthusiasm and vigor of the South in bloom, thinking of many sweet dreams under the banana tree, the scene of snatching black lychees in the lychee forest, the tone slowly becomes sad and trembling!

Happy, the moonlit night in the South!

A group of children in a small boat on the sea flew away, singing the Moonlight Night song of the South and rowing their oars quickly.

Guangzhou's Gambling Dens 202

— Bai Xia

At the beginning of the Guangdong government's reform, the central government ordered the immediate and strict prohibition of opium and gambling. Opium and gambling have a long history in Guangdong Province, and the province's annual revenue largely depends on the opium and gambling donations and taxes, so Yu Hanmou telegraphed the central government requesting a temporary reprieve. Although the prohibition of opium and gambling in Guangdong has been temporarily postponed, it is only a matter of time. In the near future, there will always be a day when it is completely banned, because the general progressive public in Guangdong have all hated opium and gambling, and in fact, the harm of opium and gambling has indeed been severe!

Guangzhou's gambling dens are institutions specially set up for gamblers, and are also commonly referred to as "Fantan Dens." Before the Northern Expedition, most of these gambling dens were located in the city of Guangzhou, but because they were unsightly, they were all moved to Henan, across the river from Guangzhou. Henan was originally an undeveloped area, but since the gambling dens were completely established in Henan, it has been transformed into a prosperous area. The so-called prosperity means that there are many more restaurants and teahouses, and some special opium dens specially set up for gamblers have also been added. A Zhujiang iron bridge was built the year before last, making transportation between Guangzhou and Henan more convenient, so the business of Henan's gambling dens, restaurants, teahouses, etc. is also more prosperous than before.

Guangzhou's gambling dens have always been contracted by the Defense Expenses Bureau, that is, all the donations and taxes are borne by the Defense Expenses Bureau organized by merchants, and the government does not care about the profits and losses of the gambling dens. After the Defense Expenses Bureau contracted, it was then parceled out to small gambling merchants, but since Chen Jitang came to power, Guangzhou's gambling dens have formed a trust, that is, contracted and operated solely by Huo Zhiting. Huo Zhiting is a big opium and gambling boss in Guangdong. The name of the trust company he uses to control the gambling dens is called "Yutai Company." As long as we arrive in Guangzhou, we can easily see many large signs on the river bank with the words "Yutai Genpai Company." These large characters also emit neon light at night, making the Guangzhou river channel even more beautiful.

Gambling dens are divided into Genpai and Qiantan. Genpai is a large gambling institution, and they accept as much money as the gamblers bet. Qiantan is a place for small gambling, and the gamblers are all coolies and small workers. As long as they have a few copper coins, they can gamble. After Huo Zhiting took over Guangzhou's gambling dens, he set up countless gambling dens, distributed in the streets and alleys of Henan. These gambling dens all have the same name, which is "Yutai Company."

"Fantan" is a unique gambling form in Guangdong, very similar to "Yabao" in the north. But "Fantan" has as many as four doors, namely one, two, three, and four. The person opening the gambling uses dice made of porcelain or copper (also old copper coins). The "Sha Tan" (the person opening the gambling) grabs a handful of dice and covers it under a specially made cup, and the gamblers can bet at will. If the number you bet on is "one," and the dice that is opened is also "one," then you have won. If you bet on "one" alone, this is called "Gu Fan," and one dollar can be paid three dollars, but after deducting a 10% discount, you can get three dollars and seventy cents including the principal. If you bet on "Jiao," that is, bet on two numbers at the same time, then it is only one dollar for one dollar, and you have to give a 10% discount. In addition, there are so-called "Lian," "Sanmen," etc. betting methods, which can be said to be numerous.

The people who work in the gambling den, in addition to the "Sha Tan," there is also the "Yintai" who keeps the money, which is equivalent to the accounting room; and there is also the "Da He," who is specially responsible for collecting money and paying money. This kind of person must be very smart in teaching before he can be competent; and there is also the "Diao Luo," who is specially responsible for using a basket to hang the gambling money of the noble gamblers upstairs to the gambling table below.

Those who can run upstairs to gamble must be big gamblers. They often bet tens of dollars, hundreds of dollars, or even thousands of dollars. The gambling den treats these people with special courtesy. As soon as they step on the second floor, the tea boy will send tea, send cigarettes, send melon seeds, send green fruits, and sometimes send snacks. In short, they try their best to please the gamblers, so that even if they lose money gambling, they feel that they have had a moment of happy life.

Because the gambling den can give a 10% discount, it always wins money. Huo Zhiting can accumulate tens of millions of wealth, all relying on gambling dens to earn it. However, the gambling den's treatment of its staff is not very harsh. Usually, each staff member only works twice a day, four hours each time. The "Sha Tan" can get a salary of one dollar and fifty cents a day, and the "Diao Luo" and "Changtai" are all one dollar and fifty cents. The "Da He" is divided into head and second hand, the head is one dollar and eighty cents, and the second hand is one dollar and fifty cents. But Daozhong's salary is not fixed, it depends on the position of this gambling den. If this gambling den is second-class, the salary will be even lower. This is talking about Genpai, as for those who work on Qiantan, the salary is much lower!

The Phoenix Returns to Its Nest 203

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Five: Jinxi's Words Repeatedly Paint Emerald Leaves; The Wedding Dress Shakes, Tears Stain the Gauze

Because his letter had a more sincere expression, the uneasy attitude when he had not seen a reply can be imagined. Now, going to meet him face to face, seeing that there was no anger on my face, he would think that I had accepted his sincere expression. Under this kind of considerate mood, he became more and more of a like-minded friend to Guoqi. But all the way to the entrance of my school, I didn't see Guoqi's trace. At that time, I was thinking that it was common for us to miss each other due to differences in time, so I would wait for the next time. On this day, as usual, when I was unhappy, I was unwilling to go home for lunch. But today, in order to get a chance to see him, I still came home to eat. Unexpectedly, the more he wanted to meet Guoqi, the less he could meet him. I went home in the evening. Looking at the faces of the people at home, it seemed that there was a secret hidden inside. He also put on a straight face, not looking anyone in the eye, and went upstairs with his schoolbag. When he passed the entrance of the main room where his mother lived, Mrs. Jiang saw him. From afar, she called out, "Menglan, you're back late. Do you have a lot of homework today?" He stopped and answered softly. Mrs. Jiang said, "Come here, I've saved you a little something you like to eat." When he spoke, he was smiling slightly, and he just kept nodding. From this, it can be seen how he wanted to express his mother-son love. Menglan couldn't bear to refuse his mother's call, so he still carried his schoolbag and went to his mother's room. Mrs. Jiang opened his wardrobe, took out a porcelain jar, put it on the table, and smiled at Menglan, "Child, guess what's in here?" Menglan shook his head and didn't answer what it was. Mrs. Jiang glanced at him. Although she had already seen that he was very unhappy, she didn't want to say anything. She opened the porcelain jar lid and smiled, "This is pine nut candy brought from Suzhou. Don't you like to eat it?" Saying that, she grabbed a handful and gave it to him. He took it with his hands and bowed awkwardly, thanking his mother. It was an unprecedented behavior. Without waiting for his mother to speak again, he turned around and went upstairs. When he got to the room, he first threw the pine nut candy on the table, then threw the schoolbag on the bed, and then leaned against the table, sitting sideways, only raising one hand to support his head. He sat there blankly until dinner before going downstairs. When eating at the table, his sister-in-law also became polite, and sent a bowl of rice that he loved to eat to him. He couldn't help laughing, "Why are you all being polite to me? Have I suddenly become a guest?" The sister-in-law smiled, "Although you are not a guest..." With just this sentence, Mrs. Jiang had already given him two glances in a row. Because of this, everyone was silent and didn't bring up...
